ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 10-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Commercial use means a use of any airplane for which a charge is made, either directly or indirectly. 
Private hangar means a hangar owned by any person other than the city. For the purposes of this chapter, if such private hangar is owned other than by one person, the owners shall designate in writing one person as the agent to deal with the city. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-28, 7-8-1982)
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2  
Secs. 10-2—10-30. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - ADMINISTRATION 
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference— Administration, ch. 2  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Secs. 10-31—10-50. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - AIRPORT BOARD 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (3) --- 
Cross reference— Boards, committees, commissions, § 2-31 et seq. 
Sec. 10-51. - Created. 
There is created in and for the city an administrative department to be designated as the airport board. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-10, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-52. - Membership. 
The airport board shall be composed of five members. Two members shall be nonpilots, and three members shall be pilots. One of the five members shall be a member of the city council. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-11, 7-8-1982; Ord. No. 1994-0010, § 1, 8-23-1994) 
Sec. 10-53. - Appointment of members. 
The members of the airport board shall be appointed by a majority vote of the city council. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-12, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-54. - Members to be citizens. 
Each member of the airport board shall be a resident citizen of the city unless such citizenship shall be waived by a majority vote of the city council. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-13, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-55. - Terms of members. 
The term of office of the members of the airport board shall commence on February 1, except for the filling of vacancies. The members shall be appointed for a term of two years, with the exception of two members whose terms shall expire on January 31, 1983, and three members whose terms shall expire on January 31, 1984. Thereafter, all members shall be appointed for terms of two years. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-14, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-56. - Compensation of members. 
The members of the airport board shall serve without compensation. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-15, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-57. - Removal of members from office. 
Any member of the airport board shall be subject to removal from office by the city council for any cause deemed sufficient by the council in the interest of public service. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-16, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-58. - Filling of vacancies. 
All vacancies occurring in the membership of the airport board shall be filled by appointment by a majority vote of the city council and for the unexpired term of the vacancy. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-17, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-59. - Organization. 
The members of the airport board shall organize and select officers of such board from its membership. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-18, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-60. - Meetings. 
The members of the airport board shall hold such meetings as the board may determine, or shall meet at the request of the city council or the city manager. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-19, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-61. - Rules of procedure, record of proceedings. 
The airport board shall adopt its own rules of procedure and keep a record of its proceedings. A copy of such record shall be filed with the city secretary. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-20, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-62. - Quorum. 
A simple majority of the members of the airport board shall constitute a quorum of the board for the transaction of all business. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-21, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-63. - Powers and duties. 
The powers and duties of the airport board shall be as follows: 
(1)	Oversee annual yet continuous operations and maintenance functions, to include:
a.	Recommendation and approval of airport specific regulations;
b.	Supervise and establish priorities for maintenance and upgrading projects;
c.	Conduct periodic safety inspections of the airport; and
d.	Receive credentials, establish qualifications, evaluate and recommend hiring of airport caretaker or manager; 
(2)	To approve all applications for the construction of hangars on airport property, and file copy with the city secretary; 
(3)	To make recommendations to the city council relative to rates to be charged for the various uses of the airport; 
(4)	Prepare, review and update long-range plan for airport development, to include:
a.	Capital improvement program, including federal-state-local funding anticipated;
b.	Operations and maintenance plans;
c.	Recommendations to local planning and zoning authority for protection of the airport through zoning for obstructions and compatible land use; 
d.	Promote orderly but compatible development of adjacent land to its maximum revenue-generating capacity; 
(5)	To consider such other items as may be referred to it by the council pertaining to the airport; and 
(6)	Serve as communications conduit for airport-related matters, to include:
a.	Provide accurate information on facilities to federal, state and city agencies;
b.	Provide liaison between the airport users and government officials;
c.	Resolve conflicts which may periodically develop between the airport and its neighbors.
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-22, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-64. - Recommendations subject to city council. 
All rules or regulations of the airport board shall be subject to modification or veto by the city council. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-23, 7-8-1982) 
Secs. 10-65—10-100. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - REGULATIONS  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Sec. 10-101. - Name of airport. 
The airport owned by the city shall be called "Fox Stephens Field-Gilmer Municipal Airport." 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-1, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-102. - Operation of vehicles on runways restricted. 
No person shall drive or operate an automotive motor vehicle upon the runways of the municipal airport owned by the city except emergency vehicles or repair vehicles. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-2, 7-8-1982)
Cross reference— Traffic and vehicles, ch. 86  
Sec. 10-103. - Possession, consumption of alcoholic beverages on city property. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to have, store, possess or consume any intoxicating beverages or liquors upon properties owned by the city and used for municipal airport purposes. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-3, 7-8-1982)
Cross reference— Alcoholic beverages, § 18-31 et seq.  
Sec. 10-104. - Hunting, use of dangerous weapons on airport property. 
It shall be unlawful for any person, except authorized city employees, to hunt, carry firearms, or hunting equipment or discharge any firearm within or upon any portion of the municipal airport property. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-4, 7-8-1982)
Cross reference— Weapons, § 54-31 et seq.  
Sec. 10-105. - Animals upon runways. 
It shall be unlawful for any person, except authorized city employees, to ride or cause to be ridden or driven any animals upon the runways of the municipal airport property. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-5, 7-8-1982)
Cross reference— Animals, ch. 6  
Secs. 10-106—10-140. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - HANGARS 
 
Sec. 10-141. - Planes based at airport generally. 
The airport board may make reasonable charges or use fees on all planes based at or using the municipal hangar or airport. A schedule of these charges shall be filed with the city manager from time to time as they are made or changed. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-29, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-142. - Authority of chair of airport board. 
The chair may, from time to time, sign ground leases with persons desiring to construct hangars on the grounds of the municipal airport, which leases shall contain, among other provisions, the provisions of this article. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-30, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-143. - Term. 
The term of any lease for hangar space at the municipal airport shall be for a period not in excess of ten years from October 1, with an option to renew the lease by the owner of the building on a year-to-year term. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-31, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-144. - Annual rent. 
The lease for airport hangar space shall provide an annual rental payable to the city on or before January 10 of each calendar year in an amount which is on file in the city secretary's office. If the lease is signed at a time other than January 1, the rental for the remainder of that year shall be prorated. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-32, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-145. - Use of hangar building. 
The airport hangar space lease shall provide that the buildings shall be used for the storage of airplanes and such other uses as may be beneficial to the best aviation interest of the city, but all leases shall specifically specify the use to which any hangar will be placed; and no owner of a hangar shall place the hangar to any use not stated in the lease or amendments to the lease. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-33, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-146. - Plans and specifications to be approved. 
Any person desiring to construct a hangar on airport land shall furnish a complete set of plans and specifications to the airport board and shall not commence any construction or moving material to the site until such time as the plans and specifications shall be approved by the airport board and a building permit has been secured and the fee paid to the city. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-34, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-147. - Execution. 
Any lease for hangar space at the municipal airport shall not be signed until the building has been constructed; and when it is completed, if it has been built in accordance with the plans and specifications, the lease shall be executed. If such hangar is not built in accordance with plans and specifications, the city inspector and the airport board shall require such to be done; and if the owner refuses to complete the construction in accordance with plans and specifications, the owner shall immediately remove the hangar; otherwise it may be demolished and removed by the city at the owner's expense. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-35, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-148. - Removal, demolition. 
All leases shall contain a provision to the effect that if the land on which the hangar is located is required by the city to be used in any airport improvement, the owner will, within 30 days after notice from the city, remove the hangar at the owner's expense; and should he fail to do so, the city may demolish and remove the hangar at the owner's expense. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-36, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-149. - Transfer of title. 
Any owner selling or transferring title to a hangar will give notice of such sale or transfer to the city manager, and the transferee shall sign a statement that the transferee assumes the obligations of the lease. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-37, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-150. - Maintenance; abatement of nuisance. 
(a)	The owner of a hangar is bound and obligated to keep the hangar in good repair at all times; keep the hangar in a sightly condition; not permit the accumulation of any cans, rubbish or other debris in or around the hangar; keep the hangar securely closed except when going in or out of the hangar; pay the rent when due; obey all rules, regulations and ordinances promulgated by the city or the airport board relating to the use of the airport; and not permit or do anything that will create a nuisance or a disturbance at the airport. 
(b)	A continued violation of this division for a period of 15 days after notice from the city manager shall void the contract and the owner shall immediately sell or transfer or remove the hangar. Upon his failure to do so, the city may demolish and remove the hangar at the expense of the owner. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-38, 7-8-1982) 
Sec. 10-151. - Lease not to be issued to persons in debt to city. 
No lease for hangar space shall be granted any person who may be indebted to the city, its lessee or agent, on any airport charges. If after a lease is granted the holder becomes delinquent for as much as 60 days in airport charges to the city, its lessee or agent, the lease shall be canceled. The city shall have a lien on the hangar for all delinquent airport charges. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0014, § 3A-39, 7-8-1982) 
Secs. 10-152—10-200. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE IV. - GILMER MUNICIPAL AIRPORT—FOX STEPHENS FIELD HAZARD ZONING REGULATIONS 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (4) --- 
Editor's note—Ord. No. 2005-011, §§ 1—15, 17, 18, adopted November 17, 2005, did not specify manner of inclusion; hence, inclusion as article IV, §§ 10-201—10-217, is at the discretion of the editor. 
Sec. 10-201. - Short title. 
These regulations shall be known and may be cited as the "Gilmer Municipal Airport-Fox Stephens Field Hazard Zoning Regulations." 
(Ord. No. 2005-011, § 1, 11-17-2005) 
Sec. 10-202. - Definitions. 
As used in these regulations, unless the context otherwise requires: 
Administrative agency means the appropriate person or office of a political subdivision which is responsible for the administration and enforcement of the regulations prescribed herein. The administrative agency is set forth in section 10-203. 
Airport means the Gilmer Municipal Airport-Fox Stephens Field, Gilmer, Texas; including the ultimate development of that facility. 
Airport elevation means The established elevation of the highest point on the runway, either existing or planned, at the airport measured in feet above mean sea level (MSL). The airport elevation of the Gilmer Municipal Airport-Fox Stephens Field is 415 feet above mean sea level (MSL). 
Airport hazard means any structure, tree, or use of land which obstructs the airspace required for the flight of aircraft or obstructs or interferes with the control, tracking, and/or data acquisition in the landing, takeoff, or flight at an airport or any installation or facility relating to flight, tracking, and/or data acquisition of the flight craft; is hazardous to, interferes with, or obstructs such landing, takeoff, or flight of aircraft; or is hazardous to or interferes with tracking and/or data acquisition pertaining to flight and flight vehicles. 
Approach surface means a surface longitudinally centered on the extended runway centerline, extending outward and upward from each end of the primary surface and at the same slope as the approach zone height limitation slope set forth in section 10-205. In plan, the perimeter of the approach surface coincides with the perimeter of the approach zone. 
Approach, conical, horizontal, and transitional zones. These zones are set forth in section 10-204. 
Board of adjustment means a board so designated by these regulations as provided in V.T.C.A, Local Government Code § 241.032. Provisions for the board of adjustment are set forth in section 10-209. 
Conical surface means a surface extending outward and upward from the periphery of the horizontal surface at a slope of 20 feet horizontally for each one foot vertically for a horizontal distance of 4,000 feet. 
Hazard to air navigation means an obstruction or use of land determined to have a substantial adverse effect on the safe and efficient utilization of navigable airspace. 
Height means, for the purpose of determining the height limits in all zones set forth in these regulations and shown on the hazard zoning map, the datum shall be height above mean sea level (MSL) elevation as measured in feet. 
Horizontal surface means a horizontal plane 150 feet above the established airport elevation which in plan coincides with the perimeter of the horizontal zone. 
Nonconforming use, structure, or tree means any structure, tree, or use of land which is inconsistent with the provisions of these regulations and which is existing as of the effective date of these regulations. 
Nonprecision instrument runway means a runway having an existing instrument approach procedure utilizing air navigation facilities or other equipment that provides only horizontal guidance or area type navigation equipment. This also includes a runway for which a nonprecision instrument approach procedure has been approved or planned. Runway 18-36 is considered a nonprecision instrument runway. 
Obstruction means any structure, tree, or other object, including a mobile object, which exceeds a limiting height set forth in section 10-205 or is an airport hazard. 
Other than utility runway means a runway designed for and intended to be used by propeller driven aircraft of more than 12,500 pounds maximum gross weight and jet powered aircraft. Runway 18-36 at the Fox Stephens Field/Gilmer Municipal Airport is considered an other than utility runway. 
Person means an individual, firm, partnership, corporation, company, association, joint stock association, or body politic and includes a trustee, receiver, assignee, administrator, executor, guardian, or other representative. 
Primary surface means a 500-foot wide surface longitudinally centered on the runway extending the full length of the ultimate runway configuration plus 200 feet beyond each ultimate end of the runway. The elevation of any point on the primary surface is the same as the nearest point on the existing or ultimate runway centerline. 
Runway means a defined area on the airport prepared for the landing and taking off of aircraft along its length. The zoned length of Runway 18-36 at the Fox Stephens Field/Gilmer Municipal Airport is 5,500 feet. 
Structure means an object, including a mobile object, constructed or installed by man including, but not limited to, buildings, towers, cranes, smokestacks, poles, earth formations, overhead power lines, and traverse ways. Traverse ways are considered to be the heights set forth in 14 C.F.R. Part 77.23. 
Transitional surfaces means surfaces extending perpendicular to the runway centerline and the extended runway centerline outward from the edges of the primary surface and the approach surfaces at a slope of seven (7) feet horizontally for each one foot vertically to where they intersect the horizontal surface. 
Tree means any type of flora and an object of natural growth. 
(Ord. No. 2005-011, § 2, 11-17-2005) 
Sec. 10-203. - Administrative agency. 
It shall be the duty of the office of city manager/community development coordinator, to administer and enforce the regulations prescribed herein and is hereby designated as the administrative agency. 
(Ord. No. 2005-011, § 3, 11-17-2005) 
Sec. 10-204. - Zones. 
In order to carry out the provisions of these regulations, there are hereby created and established certain zones which include all of the land lying beneath the approach surfaces, conical surface, horizontal surface, and transitional surfaces as they apply to the airport. Such surfaces are shown on the City of Gilmer/Gilmer Municipal Airport Hazard Zoning Map consisting of one sheet, prepared by TxDOT Aviation and dated 8-5-05, which is hereby attached to these regulations and made a part hereof. An area located in more than one of the following zones is considered to be only in the zone with the more restrictive height limitation. The various zones are hereby established and defined as follows: 
(1)	Approach zones. Approach zones are hereby established beneath the approach surfaces at each end of Runway 18-36 at the airport for an other than utility runway with non-precision instrument landings. The approach surface shall have an inner edge width of 500 feet, which coincides with the width of the primary surface, at a distance of 200 feet beyond each runway end, widening thereafter uniformly to a width of 3,500 feet at a horizontal distance of 10,000 feet beyond the end of the primary surface. The centerline of the approach surface is the continuation of the centerline of the runway. 
(2)	Conical zone. A conical zone is hereby established beneath the conical surface at the airport which extends outward from the periphery of the horizontal surface for a horizontal distance of 4,000 feet. 
(3)	Horizontal zone. A horizontal zone is hereby established beneath the horizontal surface at the airport which is a plane 150 feet above the established airport elevation, the perimeter of which is constructed by swinging arcs of 10,000 feet radii from the center of each end of the primary surface and connecting the adjacent arcs by lines tangent to those arcs. 
(4)	Transitional zones. Transitional zones are hereby established beneath the transitional surfaces at the airport. Transitional surfaces, symmetrically located on either side of the runway, have variable widths as shown on the Gilmer Municipal Airport-Fox Stephens Field Hazard Zoning Map. Transitional surfaces extend outward perpendicular to the runway centerline and the extended runway centerline from the periphery of the primary surface and the approach surfaces to where they intersect the horizontal surface. 
(Ord. No. 2005-011, § 4, 11-17-2005) 
Sec. 10-205. - Height limitations. 
Except as otherwise provided in section 10-208, no structure shall be erected, altered, or replaced and no tree shall be allowed to grow in any zone created by these regulations to a height in excess of the applicable height limitations herein established for such zone except as provided in subsection (5). Such applicable height limitations are hereby established for each of the zones in question as follows: 
(1)	Approach zones. Slope one foot in height for each 34 feet in horizontal distance beginning at the end of and at the same elevation as the primary surface and extending to a point 10,000 feet beyond the end of the primary surface. 
(2)	Conical zone. Slopes one foot in height for each 20 feet in horizontal distance beginning at the periphery of the horizontal zone and at 150 feet above the airport elevation and extending to a height of 350 feet above the airport elevation, or to a height of 765.0 feet above mean sea level. 
(3)	Horizontal zone. Established at 150 feet above the airport elevation, or at a height of 565.0 feet above mean sea level. 
(4)	Transitional zones. Slope one foot in height for each seven feet in horizontal distance beginning at the sides of and at the same elevations as the primary surface and the approach surfaces. 
(5)	Excepted height limitation. Nothing contained in these regulations shall be construed as prohibiting the growth, construction, or maintenance of any structure or tree to a height of up to 50 feet above the surface of the land at its location. 
(Ord. No. 2005-011, § 5, 11-17-2005) 
Sec. 10-206. - Land use restrictions. 
Except as provided in section 10-207, no use may be made of land or water within any zone established by these regulations in such a manner as to create electrical interference with navigational signals or radio communications between the airport and aircraft, make it difficult for pilots to distinguish between airport lights and others, result in glare in the eyes of pilots using the airport, impair visibility in the vicinity of the airport, create potential bird strike hazards, or otherwise in any way endanger or interfere with the landing, taking off, or maneuvering of aircraft intending to use the airport. 
(Ord. No. 2005-011, § 6, 11-17-2005) 
Sec. 10-207. - Nonconforming uses, structures, and trees. 
(a)	Nonconforming uses. Nothing contained in these regulations shall be construed as requiring changes in or interference with the continuance of any nonconforming use of land. 
(b)	Nonconforming structures. Nothing contained in these regulations shall be construed as to require the removal, lowering, or other change to any existing nonconforming structure including all phases or elements of a multiphase structure the construction of which was begun prior to the effective date of these regulations and is diligently prosecuted. 
(c)	Nonconforming trees. Nothing in these regulations shall be construed as to require the removal, lowering, or other change to any nonconforming tree. However, any nonconforming tree which grows to a greater height than it was as of the effective date of these regulations is subject to the provisions of these regulations as described in section 10-205 
(Ord. No. 2005-011, § 7, 11-17-2005) 
Sec. 10-208. - Permits and variances. 
(a)	Permits. Any person who desires to replace, rebuild, substantially change, or repair a nonconforming structure or replace or replant a nonconforming tree must apply for and receive a permit, and the permit shall be granted. However, no permit shall be granted which would allow the establishment of an airport hazard or allow a nonconforming structure or tree to exceed its original height or become a greater hazard to air navigation than it was at the time of the adoption of these regulations. Applications for permit shall be applied to and issued by the administrative agency. 
(b)	Variances. Any person who desires to erect, substantially change, or increase the height of any structure or establish or allow the growth of any tree which would exceed the height limitations set forth in section 10-205 or change the use of property in such a way as to create a hazardous condition as described in section 10-206 must apply to the board of adjustment and receive a variance. The application for variance must be accompanied by a determination from the Federal Aviation Administration under 14 C.F.R. Part 77 as to the effect of the proposal on the operation of air navigation facilities and the safe, efficient use of navigable airspace. Such variances shall be allowed where it is duly found that a literal application or enforcement of the regulations will result in practical difficulty or unnecessary hardship and the granting of relief would result in substantial justice, not be contrary to the public interest, and be in accordance with the spirit of these regulations. 
(c)	Requirements and reasonable conditions. 
(1)	Any permit granted may, at the discretion of the administrative agency, impose a requirement to allow the installation and maintenance, at the expense of the administrative agency, of any markers or lights as may be necessary to indicate to flyers the presence of an airport hazard. 
(2)	Any variance granted may, at the discretion of the board of adjustment, impose any reasonable conditions as may be necessary to accomplish the purpose of these regulations. 
(Ord. No. 2005-011, § 8, 11-17-2005) 
Sec. 10-209. - Board of adjustment. 
(a)	The board of adjustment of the city is hereby designated as the board of adjustment for the purposes of these regulations and shall have and exercise the following powers: 
(1)	To hear and decide appeals from any order, requirement, decision, or determination made by the administrative agency in the administration or enforcement of these regulations; 
(2)	To hear and decide special exceptions to the terms of these regulations when the board is required to do so; and 
(3)	To hear and decide specific variances.
(b)	The board of adjustment shall be comprised of five members and shall adopt rules for its governance and procedure in harmony with the provisions of these regulations. Meetings of the board of adjustment shall be held at the call of the chairman and at such times as the board of adjustment may determine. The chairman, or in his/her absence the acting chairman, may administer oaths and compel the attendance of witnesses. All hearings of the board of adjustment shall be public. The board of adjustment shall keep minutes of its proceedings showing the vote of each member upon each question or if any member is absent or fails to vote, indicating such fact and shall keep records of its examinations and other official actions, all of which shall immediately be filed in the office of the board of adjustment or in the office of community development coordinator [of the] city. All such records shall be public records. 
(c)	The board of adjustment shall make written findings of fact and conclusions of law stating the facts upon which it relied when making its legal conclusions in reversing, affirming, or modifying any order, requirement, decision, or determination which comes before it under the provisions of these regulations. 
(d)	The concurring vote of four members of the board of adjustment shall be necessary to reverse any order, requirement, decision, or determination of the administrative agency, to decide in favor of the applicant on any matter upon which it is required to pass under these regulations, or to effect any variance to these regulations. 
(Ord. No. 2005-011, § 9, 11-17-2005) 
Sec. 10-210. - Appeals. 
(a)	Any person aggrieved or any taxpayer affected by a decision of the administrative agency made in the administration of these regulations may appeal to the board of adjustment if that person or taxpayer is of the opinion that a decision of the administrative agency is an improper application of these regulations. This same right of appeal is extended to the governing bodies of the city and Upshur County, Texas, and to the City of Gilmer-Upshur County Joint Airport Zoning Board. 
(b)	All appeals hereunder must be taken within a reasonable time as provided by the rules of the board of adjustment by filing a notice of appeal with the board of adjustment and the administrative agency specifying the grounds for the appeal. The administrative agency shall forthwith transmit to the board of adjustment all papers constituting the record upon which the action appealed was taken. 
(c)	An appeal shall stay all proceedings in furtherance of the action appealed unless the administrative agency certifies in writing to the board of adjustment that by reason of the facts stated in the certificate, a stay would, in the opinion of the administrative agency, cause imminent peril to life or property. In such case, proceedings shall not be stayed except by order of the board of adjustment on notice to the administrative agency and on due cause shown. 
(d)	The board of adjustment shall fix a reasonable time for hearing appeals, give public notice and due notice to the parties in interest, and decide the same within a reasonable time. Upon the hearing, any party may appear in person, by agent, and/or by attorney. 
(e)	The board of adjustment may reverse or affirm, in whole or in part, or modify the administrative agency's order, requirement, decision, or determination from which an appeal is taken and make the correct order, requirement, decision, or determination, and for this purpose the board of adjustment has the same authority as the administrative agency. 
(Ord. No. 2005-011, § 10, 11-17-2005) 
Sec. 10-211. - Judicial review. 
Any person aggrieved or any taxpayer affected by a decision of the board of adjustment may present to a court of record a petition stating that the decision of the board of adjustment is illegal and specifying the grounds of the illegality as provided by and in accordance with the provisions of Texas Local Government Code, § 241.041. This same right of appeal is extended to the governing bodies of the city, and Upshur County, Texas, and to the City of Gilmer-Upshur County Joint Airport Zoning Board. 
(Ord. No. 2005-011, § 11, 11-17-2005) 
Sec. 10-212. - Enforcement and remedies. 
The governing bodies of the city or Upshur County, Texas, or the City of Gilmer-Upshur County Joint Airport Zoning Board may institute in a court of competent jurisdiction an action to prevent, restrain, correct, or abate any violation of these regulations or of any order or ruling made in connection with their administration or enforcement including, but not limited to, an action for injunctive relief. 
(Ord. No. 2005-011, § 12, 11-17-2005) 
Sec. 10-213. - Penalties. 
Each violation of these regulations or of any order or ruling promulgated hereunder shall constitute a misdemeanor and upon conviction shall be punishable by a fine of not more than $200.00 and each day a violation continues to exist shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. 2005-011, § 13, 11-17-2005) 
Sec. 10-214. - Conflicting regulations. 
Where there exists a conflict between any of the regulations or limitations prescribed herein and any other regulation applicable to the same area, whether the conflict be with respect to the height of structures or trees, the use of land, or any other matter, the more stringent limitation or requirement shall control. 
(Ord. No. 2005-011, § 14, 11-17-2005) 
Sec. 10-215. - Severability. 
If any of the provisions of these regulations or the application thereof to any person or circumstance is held invalid, such invalidity shall not affect other provisions or application of these regulations which can be given effect without the invalid provision or application and to this end, the provisions of these regulations are declared to be severable. 
(Ord. No. 2005-011, § 15, 11-17-2005) 
Sec. 10-216. - Duties of joint airport zoning board. 
Sixty days following the date of adoption of this article, the duties, responsibilities and authority of the City of Gilmer-Upshur County Joint Airport Zoning Board shall be dissolved. 
(Ord. No. 2005-011, § 17, 11-17-2005) 
Sec. 10-217. - Adherence with state laws. 
Any actions brought forth by any person or taxpayer as a result of the administration, enforcement, or the contesting these regulations will be in accordance with the provisions of V.T.C.A, Local Government Code, §§ 241.001 et seq. and other applicable state laws. 
(Ord. No. 2005-011, § 18, 11-17-2005)

DIVISION 2. - ELECTRICAL 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference— Utilities, ch. 90  
Sec. 14-51. - Installation standards. 
(a)	All installations shall be in strict conformity with the provisions of this division, the statutes of the state, the rules and regulations issued under authority of the state statutes, and shall be in conformity with approved standards of construction for safety to life and property. In every case where no specific type or class of material or no specific standard of construction is prescribed by the statutes of the state, the regulations issued under the authority of the state statutes or by this division, conformity with the regulations as laid down in the National Electrical Code, as approved by the American Standards Association; and other installation and safety regulations approved by the American Standards Association shall be prima facie evidence of conformity with approved standards of construction for safety to life and property. 
(b)	All electrical equipment installed or used shall be in conformity with the provisions of this division; the statutes of the state and any order, rules and regulations issued by authority of this division and such statutes and with approved electrical standards for safety to persons and property. Unless by this division, by a statute of the state, or by any orders, rules or regulations issued by authority of this division and such statutes, a specific type or class of electrical equipment is disapproved for installation and use, conformity with the standards of Underwriters' Laboratories, Inc., as approved by the American Standards Association, shall be prima facie evidence of conformity with approved standards for safety to persons and property; however, the provisions of this division shall not apply to equipment owned and used by an electrical supply or communications agency, in the generation, transmission or distribution of electricity or for the operation of signals or the transmission of intelligence. 
(c)	No electrical apparatus, fitting or material shall be used or placed on sale unless such apparatus, fitting or material is approved by the electrical inspector as complying with the safety requirements of this division; however, all such apparatus, fittings or material which bears the label of Underwriters' Laboratories, Inc., shall be deemed prima facie evidence to satisfy the requirements of this division; and the electrical inspector is authorized to approve such apparatus, fittings and material without requiring that further tests be made. 
(d)	Approved wiring methods are as follows:
(1)	Rigid metal conduit.
(2)	Electrical metallic tubing.
(3)	Flexible metal conduit.
(4)	Surface metal raceways.
(5)	Underfloor raceways.
(6)	Cellular metal floor raceways.
(7)	Wireways.
(8)	Busways.
(9)	Service entrance cable.
(10)	Open wiring insulators.
(11)	Nonmetallic sheathed cable.
(12)	Or any other method approved by the National Electrical Code, with the exception of the use of aluminum wire. 
(e)	The term "fire limits," as referred to in the provisions of this division relating to electrical work within the fire limits of the city, shall be taken to mean and include the district contained within the fire limits or districts as they exist at the time of the installation or performance of such electrical work. 
(f)	All wiring other than residential and multifamily shall be in electrical conduit, surface metal raceways, underfloor raceways, cellular metal, floor raceways, wireways, busways. 
(g)	Switchboards, switches, panel boards, control boards and distributing centers of any and all types shall be dead-front safety-type equipment located in machinery rooms which are safeguarded as provided for elevator-control equipment. 
(h)	All panels and switchboards used for the control of lighting and appliance circuits in residential and commercial buildings shall be of the multibreaker type. All switches, disconnects, circuit breakers, load centers, and multibreakers when mounted outside and exposed to the weather shall be raintight, designed for outdoor service. 
(i)	Ground fault circuit interrupters are now required for all unfinished accessory buildings used for storage or work areas when associated with dwellings for any readily accessible general use receptacles. 
(j)	All outdoor receptacles for dwellings are required to be ground fault circuit interrupters protected. 
(k)	Outdoor receptacles cannot be on small appliance circuits.
(l)	Bathroom receptacles are required to be on at least one separate 20-amp branch circuit that serves only bathroom receptacles. 
(m)	Service disconnect and overcurrent protection shall not be located in a bathroom.
(n)	The grounded conductor is no longer permitted under any conditions to serve as the equipment grounding conductor for new installations. 
(o)	Receptacles shall not be located in bathtubs and shower spaces.
(p)	Lighting tracks and ceiling fans above in an area above the tub measured three feet horizontally and eight feet vertically from the top of the bathtub rim is prohibited. 
(q)	All 125-volt receptacles located within five feet of a hydromassage bathtub shall be protected. 
(r)	Metal-clad cable may be used in remodels where electrical conduit is not practical. All flexible conduit shall have a ground wire. 
(s)	All smoke alarms shall be hard wired in commercial and residential buildings, and no batteries will be allowed except for emergency backup. 
(Ord. No. 1997-0004, 4-10-1997) 
Secs. 14-52—14-70. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 3. - PLUMBING 
 
Sec. 14-71. - Duties of the plumbing inspector. 
(a)	It shall be the duty of the plumbing inspector, under the direction of the city manager to: 
(1)	Sign and issue all notices and certificates and to pass on all plans submitted;
(2)	Keep a daily record of his work, including all notices and applications received, violations of this division and all other pertinent matters; 
(3)	Make daily, weekly and quarterly reports and annual reports to the city council;
(4)	Inspect all houses in course of erection, alteration and repair, as often as may be necessary; and 
(5)	See that all work for plumbing, drainage and ventilation is done in accordance with the provisions of this division. 
(b)	The plumbing inspector will inspect all sewer connections and external house drains within five hours after notification by the plumber, Saturdays, Sundays and holidays excepted, and all waste and vent pipes and other inside plumbing within 24 hours after notification, Saturdays, Sundays and holidays excepted. 
(c)	Should the plumbing inspector fail to comply with the requirements of this section, the plumber doing the work shall file with the health officer a written statement that the inspection was not made within the time mentioned in this section. 
(d)	The fee for inspection of all water, sewer, water heater and gas lines is on file in the city secretary's office. This fee is to be paid upon application for a permit. For all inspection trips to the job over and above one trip, there shall be a charge on file in the city secretary's office for each trip. 
(e)	The plumbing board may permit the installations being made though some may conflict with this division if in its judgment the work, material and methods prescribe equal or better safety from a sanitary standpoint. 
(Ord. No. 1996-0017, § 1, 8-29-1996) 
Sec. 14-72. - General plumbing rules. 
Each person doing business as a plumber or drainlayer or property owner personally doing or performing his own work, must conform to the following rules and regulations: Before beginning any work, all of the applicable requirements mentioned in this article must be complied with and a permit issued for such work must be in the possession of that person making application for such permit; and no person conducting a plumbing business shall allow his name to be used by any person directly or indirectly to obtain a permit to do any work under his bond. The charge for plumbing permits is on file in the city secretary's office. 
(Ord. No. 1996-0017, § 2, 8-29-1996) 
Sec. 14-73. - Interceptors and separators (grease traps). 
(a)	Wastes from kitchen sinks, and/or dishwashers in any hotel, restaurant, clubhouse, boardinghouse, public institution, hospital or other establishments where grease can be introduced into the drainage system in quantities that can effect line stoppage or hinder sewage disposal shall discharge into an approved type grease trap of adequate size before entering the sanitary drain or sewer. The grease trap shall be properly vented; and if it is more than four feet horizontally or 30 inches vertically from the outlet of the fixtures it serves, the fixture shall have a separate trap and vent. The grease-retaining capacity of each grease trap in pounds of grease shall be equal to twice the rate of flow capacity in gallons per minute of wastewater so that the trap shall remove and retain 90 percent of the grease discharged into it up to its required capacity of accumulated grease. For calculating the required sizes of grease traps, the rate of discharge from each fixture connected to the trap shall be based upon the rates shown in the following table: 
Type of Fixture 	Rate of Flow
in gpm 
Single compartment sink with 1½-inch waste .....	15 
Double compartment sink with 1½-inch waste .....	20
Triple compartment sink with 2-inch waste .....	25
Dishwashers:	
	Up to 30 gallon water capacity .....	15 
	Up to 50 gallon water capacity .....	25
	Up to 100 gallon water capacity .....	40
Floor drain, each .....	 5
 
(b)	Interceptors or separators shall be provided where they are necessary for the proper handling of wastes containing ingredients harmful to the building system, the public sewer or sewage treatment plant or processes. 
(c)	Each interceptor (grease trap) shall be so installed as to provide ready accessibility to the cover and means for servicing and maintaining the interceptor in working and operating condition. 
(d)	Interceptors shall be maintained in efficient operating condition by periodic removal of accumulated grease. Establishments must provide the city water superintendent or the city inspector with receipts for waste collections. 
(Ord. No. 1996-0006, art. II, 2-8-1996) 
Secs. 14-74—14-100. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - DANGEROUS BUILDINGS 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (3) --- 
Charter reference— Dangerous structures, § 11.08 
Cross reference— Environment, ch. 34  
Sec. 14-101. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Dangerous building means any building or structure which has any of the following defects or is in any of the following conditions; however, this enumeration shall not be deemed or construed to be conclusive, limiting or restrictive: 
(1)	Whenever any door, aisle, passageway, stairway or other means of exit does not conform to the approved fire code of the city; 
(2)	Whenever any portion has been damaged by fire, wind, flood or by any other cause in such manner that the structural strength or stability is appreciably less than it was before such catastrophe and is less than the minimum requirements of the building code of the city for a new building or similar structure, purpose or location; 
(3)	Whenever any portion or member or appurtenance is likely to fall or to become detached or dislodged, or to collapse and thereby injure persons or damage property; 
(4)	Whenever any portion has settled to such an extent that walls or other structural portions have materially less resistance to winds than is required in the case of new construction by the building code of the city; 
(5)	Whenever any building or structure or any part, because of dilapidation, deterioration, decay, faulty construction, or because of the removal or movement of some portion of the ground necessary for the purpose of supporting such building or portion, or some other reason, is likely to be partially or completely collapsed; 
(6)	Whenever for any reason whatsoever the building or structure or any portion is manifestly unsafe for the purpose for which it is used; 
(7)	Whenever any building or structure has been so damaged by fire, wind or flood, or has become so dilapidated or deteriorated as to become an attractive nuisance to children who might play in the building or structure to their danger, or as to afford a harborage for vagrants, criminals or immoral persons, or as to enable persons to resort to the building or structure for the purpose of committing a nuisance or unlawful or immoral acts; 
(8)	Whenever any building or structure used or intended to be used for dwelling purposes, because of dilapidation, decay, damage or faulty construction or arrangement or otherwise, is unsanitary or unfit for human habitation or is in a condition that is likely to cause sickness or disease when so determined by the health officer, or likely to work injury to the health, safety or general welfare of those living within; or 
(9)	Whenever any building becomes vacant, dilapidated and open at a door or window, leaving the interior of the building exposed to the elements or accessible to entrance by trespassers. 
(Ord. No. 1979-0013, § 9.70, 11-8-1979)
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2  
Sec. 14-102. - Unlawful to keep or maintain. 
It is unlawful for any owner or his agent to keep or maintain any building or part which is a dangerous building. 
(Ord. No. 1979-0013, § 9.71, 11-8-1979) 
Sec. 14-103. - Notice of hearing. 
(a)	When the whole or any part of any building or structure is found to be in a dangerous or unsafe condition, the building inspector shall issue a notice of the dangerous and unsafe condition. 
(b)	Such notice shall be directed to each owner of or party in interest in the building in whose name the property appears on the last local tax assessment records. 
(c)	The notice shall specify the time and place of a hearing on the condition of the building or structure, at which time and place the person to whom the notice is directed shall have the opportunity to show cause why the building or structure should not be ordered to be demolished or otherwise made safe. 
(d)	The building inspector shall file a copy of the notice of the dangerous and unsafe condition with the hearing officer. 
(Ord. No. 1979-0013, § 9.72, 11-8-1979) 
Sec. 14-104. - Service of notice. 
All notices served under this article shall be in writing and shall be served upon the person to whom they are directed personally, or in lieu of personal service may be mailed by certified mail, return receipt requested, addressed to such owner or party in interest at the address shown on the tax records, at least 15 days before the date of the hearing described in the notice. If any person to whom a notice is directed is not personally served, in addition to mailing the notice, a copy shall be posted upon a conspicuous part of the building or structure. 
(Ord. No. 1979-0013, § 9.73, 11-8-1979) 
Sec. 14-105. - Appointment of hearing officer. 
The hearing officer, functioning under this article, shall be appointed by the city manager to serve at the manager's pleasure. 
(Ord. No. 1979-0013, § 9.74, 11-8-1979) 
Sec. 14-106. - Hearing and order of hearing officer. 
(a)	The hearing officer shall take testimony of the building inspector, the owner of the property and any interested party at the hearing under this article. The hearing officer shall render a decision either closing the proceedings or ordering the building to be demolished or otherwise made safe. 
(b)	If it is determined by the hearing officer that the building or structure should be demolished or otherwise made safe, the hearing officer shall so order, fixing a time in the order for the owner, agent or lessee to comply with the order. 
(c)	If the owner, agent or lessee fails to appear or neglects or refuses to comply with the order, the hearing officer shall file a report of such officer's findings and a copy of such officer's order with the city council and request that the necessary action be taken to demolish or otherwise make safe the building or structure. A copy of the findings and order of the hearing officer shall be served on the owner, agent or lessee in the manner prescribed in section 14-104 
(Ord. No. 1979-0013, § 9.75, 11-8-1979) 
Sec. 14-107. - Review hearing by city council. 
The city council shall fix a date for a hearing, reviewing the findings and order of the hearing officer under section 14-106 and shall give notice to the owner, agent or lessee in the manner prescribed in section 14-104 of the time and place of the hearing. At the hearing, the owner, agent or lessee shall be given the opportunity to show cause why the building should not be demolished or otherwise made safe; and the city council shall either approve, disapprove or modify the order for the demolition or making safe of the building or structure. 
(Ord. No. 1979-0013, § 9.76, 11-8-1979) 
Sec. 14-108. - Emergency abatement by city. 
When in the opinion of the building inspector or other duly designated officer there is actual and immediate danger of failure or collapse of a building or structure or any part which would endanger life, or when any structure or part of a structure has fallen and life is endangered by the occupation of the building or structure, the building inspector is authorized and empowered to order and require the inmates and occupants to vacate the building or structure forthwith. The building inspector or other duly designated officer of the city shall proceed to demolish or make safe the dangerous building, as described in this section, and shall prepare a statement of costs incurred in such work. 
(Ord. No. 1979-0013, § 9.77, 11-8-1979) 
Sec. 14-109. - Penalty for failure or refusal to comply. 
Upon failure of the owner, upon whom notice to demolish or make safe a dangerous building was served pursuant to this article, to demolish or make safe a dangerous building, such owner shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction shall be fined as provided in section 1-14. In case the owner or occupant of any lot or premises under the provisions of this article shall be a corporation and shall violate any provision of this article, the president, vice-president, secretary, treasurer of such corporation, or any manager, agent or employee of such corporation shall be also liable for the penalties provided in this section. 
(Ord. No. 1981-0002, § 9.78, 1-5-1981) 
Sec. 14-110. - Right of city to perform work. 
If an owner refuses or fails to comply with the provisions of this article, despite penalties, or if the owner cannot be contacted, and if the violation represents an immediate threat to health or safety in the view of the mayor, city manager or city health officer, the city may perform the necessary work to eliminate the threat. 
(Ord. No. 1981-0002, § 9.80, 1-5-1981) 
Sec. 14-111. - Judicial review. 
An owner aggrieved by any final decision or order of the city council under section 14-107 may appeal the decision or order to a court of competent jurisdiction by filing a petition for an order of superintending control within 20 days from the date of the decision. 
(Ord. No. 1979-0013, § 9.79, 11-8-1979) 
Sec. 14-112. - City costs declared lien; collection as taxes. 
(a)	The cost of the demolition or making a building safe under this article shall be a lien against the real property and shall be reported to the city assessor, who shall assess the cost against the property on which the building or structure is located. 
(b)	The owner or party in interest in whose name the property appears upon the last local tax assessment records shall be notified of the amount of such cost by first class mail at the address shown on the records. If such owner or party in interest fails to pay such amount within 30 days after mailing by the assessor of the notice of the amount, the assessor shall add such amount to the next tax roll of the city; and such amount shall be collected in the same manner in all respects as provided by law for the collection of taxes by the city. 
(Ord. No. 1979-0013, § 9.80, 11-8-1979) 
Chapter 18 - BUSINESSES

ARTICLE II. - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES 
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference— Possession, consumption of alcoholic beverages on city property, § 10-103; possession or consumption of alcoholic beverages in public parks prohibited, § 62-1; consumption of alcohol prohibited on streets and sidewalks, § 74-1 
State Law reference— Alcoholic beverages, V.T.C.A., Alcoholic Beverage Code § 1.01 et seq. 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Secs. 18-31—18-50. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - NUDITY 
 
Sec. 18-51. - Purpose. 
The purpose of this division is to prohibit certain acts of commercial exploitation of human sexuality in commercial establishments within the city limits where alcoholic beverages are served or offered for sale for consumption on the premises, and to reduce the likelihood of criminal activity, moral degradation and disturbances of the peace and good order of the community, to prohibit lewd and unlawful activity, such as prostitution and the proliferation of controlled substances, all of which may occur when such commercial exploitation is permitted in such places, and to promote the preservation of property values of neighborhoods and adjacent properties. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0007, § 1, 6-16-1994) 
Sec. 18-52. - Prohibition of nudity in commercial establishments serving or permitting the consumption of alcoholic beverages. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person maintaining, owning or operating a commercial establishment located within the boundaries of the city at which alcoholic beverages are served or offered for sale for consumption on the premises, or at which alcoholic beverages are permitted to be consumed to: 
(1)	Suffer or permit any female person, while on the premises of such commercial establishment, to expose that area of the human female breast at or below the top of the areola. 
(2)	Suffer or permit any female person, while on the premises of such commercial establishment, to use any device or covering which is intended to give the appearance of or simulate such portions of the human female breasts as described in subsection (a)(1) of this section. 
(3)	Suffer or permit any person, while on the premises of such commercial establishment, to expose his genitals, pubic areas, buttocks, anus, or anal cleft or cleavage. 
(4)	Suffer or permit any person, while on the premises of such commercial establishment, to use any device or covering which is intended to give the appearance of or simulate the genitals, pubic area, buttocks, anus, or anal cleft or cleavage. 
(b)	It shall be unlawful for any female person, while on the premises of a commercial establishment located within the boundaries of the city at which alcoholic beverages are served or offered for sale for consumption on the premises, or at which alcoholic beverages are permitted to be consumed, to expose that area of the human female breast at or below the top of the areola, or to use any device or covering which is intended to give the appearance or simulate such areas of the female breast as described in this section. 
(c)	It shall be unlawful for any person, while on the premises of a commercial establishment located within the boundaries of the city at which alcoholic beverages are served or offered for sale for consumption on the premises, or at which alcoholic beverages are permitted to be consumed, to expose his genitals, pubic area, buttocks, anus, or anal cleft or cleavage, or to use any device or covering which is intended to give the appearance of or simulate the genitals, pubic area, buttocks, anus, or anal cleft or cleavage. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0007, § 1, 6-16-1994) 
Sec. 18-53. - Injunctive relief. 
The city attorney is authorized to seek compliance with this division by seeking injunctive relief in a court of proper jurisdiction to compel the operator, owner, or other violator of this division to comply with the terms and provisions of this division. The ability of the city to seek injunctive relief under this section shall not be subject to, nor shall it be a prerequisite of, that the city has sought compliance with this division of application of penalties and sanctions as otherwise set out in this division. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0007, § 1, 6-16-1994) 
Sec. 18-54. - Penalties. 
Any violation of the provisions of this division shall be punishable by fine as provided in section 1-14. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0007, § 1, 6-16-1994) 
Secs. 18-55—18-80. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 3. - LOCATION 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (3) --- 
Cross reference— Zoning, app. A. 
Sec. 18-81. - Sales near school, church or hospital. 
(a)	The sale of alcoholic beverages by a dealer whose place of business is within 300 feet of a church, public school or public hospital or 1,000 feet of a public school, if the city council receives a request from the board of trustees of a school district under V.T.C.A., Education Code § 38.007 is prohibited. 
(b)	The measurement of the distance between the place of business where alcoholic beverages are sold and the church or public hospital shall be along the property lines of the street fronts and from front door to front door, and in direct line across intersections. The measurement of the distance between the place of business where alcoholic beverages are sold and the public schools shall be in a direct line from the property line of the public school to the property line of the place of business, and in a direct line across intersections. 
(c)	Every applicant for an original alcoholic beverage license or permit for a location with a door by which the public may enter the place of business of the applicant that is within 1,000 feet of the nearest property line of a public school, measured along street lines and directly across intersections, must give written notice of the application to officials of the public school before filing the application with the city council. A copy of the notice must be submitted to the city council with the application. This subsection does not apply to a permit or license covering premises where minors are prohibited from entering the premises under V.T.C.A., Alcoholic Beverage Code § 109.53. 
(d)	As to any dealer who held a license or permit on September 1, 1983, in a location where a regulation under this section was in effect on that date, for purposes of subsection (a), but not subsection (c), of this section, the measurement of the distance between the place of business of the dealer and a public school shall be along the property lines of the street fronts and from front door to front door, and in direct line across intersections. 
(e)	The city council may also allow variances to the regulation if the council determines that enforcement of the regulation in a particular instance is not in the best interest of the public, constitutes waste or inefficient use of land or other resources, creates an undue hardship on an applicant for a license or permit, does not serve its intended purpose, is not effective or necessary, or for any other reason the council, after consideration of the health, safety and welfare of the public and the equities of the situation, determines is in the best interest of the community. 
(f)	Subsection (a) does not apply to the holder of a:
(1)	Retail on-premises consumption permit or license if less than 50 percent of the gross receipts for the premises is from the sale or service of alcoholic beverages; 
(2)	Retail off-premises consumption permit or license if less than 50 percent of the gross receipts for the premises, excluding the sale of items subject to the motor fuels tax, is from the sale or service of alcoholic beverages; or 
(3)	Wholesaler's, distributor's, brewer's, distiller's and rectifier's, winery, wine bottler's or manufacturer's permit or license, or any other license or permit held by a wholesaler or manufacturer as those words are ordinarily used and understood in V.T.C.A., Alcoholic Beverage Code § 102.001 et seq. 
(Ord. No. 1983-0023, 9-8-1983)
State Law reference— Similar provisions, V.T.C.A., Alcoholic Beverage Code § 109.33.  
Secs. 18-82—18-110. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - ELECTRICIANS 
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (4) --- 
Cross reference— Utilities, ch. 90  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Sec. 18-111. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning. Words used in the National Electrical Code shall have the meanings assigned to them in that code. Words relating to buildings and building use, when not otherwise separately defined, shall have meanings which conform to the meanings set out in the building ordinances of the city, if set out; otherwise, they shall have their usual meaning. 
Apprentice electrician means a person who is learning the trade of an electrician and who works only under the direct supervision of a journeyman electrician or master electrician and who has registered as an apprentice. 
Approved and approval mean inspected and accepted by the electrical inspector as having met the requirements of this article. 
Authorized person means an individual or authorized representative of a firm or corporation who is licensed to do work as permitted under the specific provisions of this article. 
Board of electrical examiners means the board of electrical examiners. 
Electrical inspector means the chief electrical inspector and his authorized assistants. 
Electrical work means any act in connection with the installing, altering, repairing and/or maintaining of electric wires, conduits, apparatus or other electrical installation designed or capable of carrying electrical energy, which act ordinarily requires the use of tools. 
Experience means active and practical experience during which not less than two-thirds of one's time, exclusive of normal periods of rest and recreation, has been spent in the installation, alteration and repair of electrical equipment and conductors. A bachelor's degree in electrical engineering from a college or university which requires at least four years of study in residence as a prerequisite to such degree shall be considered as the equivalent of three years of experience, and the satisfactory completion of 120 semester hours of work required for such degree shall be considered the equivalent of one year of experience. 
Journeyman electrician means a person licensed as a journeyman electrician in compliance with the requirements of this article, who works for and under the general supervision and direction of a master electrician, doing electrical work contracted for by a master electrician and who does not hold himself out to the public as being qualified to contract for the doing of electrical work. 
Master electrician means any person licensed as a master electrician in compliance with the requirements of this article, who holds himself out to the public as being qualified to do the kind of electrical work or to contract for the doing of the kind of electrical work, by himself or by the employment of journeyman electricians or apprentice electricians, which his license authorizes him to do. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0005, § 5.47, 5-13-1982)
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2  
Sec. 18-112. - Object, scope of article. 
(a)	The object of this article is to reduce the personal hazard and the fire hazard from electrical causes. To accomplish this, the requirements set forth in this article are intended to provide a minimum standard for electrical installation in the city. 
(b)	The provisions of this article shall not apply to installation in railway cars or automotive equipment or to installations used by electrical public utility, telephone, telegraph companies and radio transmission stations, in the generation, transmission or in distribution of electricity or for the operation of signals or the transmission of intelligence, in the exercise of their functions as such agencies and located outdoors, or in buildings used exclusively for that purpose; however, this article, except as to permits, shall apply to all such wiring and equipment installed in or on the consumers premises. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0005, § 5.48, 5-13-1982) 
Sec. 18-113. - Enforcement of article provisions. 
This article shall be enforced by the city electrical inspector in accordance with the interpretation contained in the National Electrical Code, a certified copy of which shall be on file in the office of the city secretary. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0005, § 5.49, 5-13-1982) 
Sec. 18-114. - Liability for damages. 
This article shall not be construed to affect the responsibility or liability of any party owning, operating, controlling or installing any electrical equipment for damages to persons or to property caused by any defect in such equipment; nor shall the city or any officer or employee of the city be held liable by reason of the inspection or reinspection authorized in this article or the certificate or disapproval of any equipment authorized in this article. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0005, § 5.50, 5-13-1982) 
Secs. 18-115—18-140. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - BOARD OF ELECTRICAL EXAMINERS 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (5) --- 
Cross reference— Boards, committees, commissions, § 2-31 et seq. 
Sec. 18-141. - Creation. 
There is created an examining, licensing, advisory and appeal board which will be known as the board of electrical examiners. The city inspector shall serve as recorder for the board of electrical examiners. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0005, § 5.51(a), 5-13-1982) 
Sec. 18-142. - Composition. 
The board of electrical examiners shall consist of five members, any three of whom shall constitute a quorum. The board shall include three licensed master electricians and two other citizens deemed advisable by the city council. The fire marshal or fire chief of the city and the electrical inspector shall be ex officio members of the board with no right to vote. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0005, § 5.51(b), 5-13-1982) 
Sec. 18-143. - Appointment. 
The board of electrical examiners shall be appointed by the city council and shall hold office for a period of two years from date of appointment or until their successors have been appointed and qualified. On the initial appointment the council may vary the terms. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0005, § 5.51(c), 5-13-1982) 
Sec. 18-144. - Compensation; chair; meetings. 
(a)	All members shall serve on the board of electrical examiners without pay.
(b)	The board shall select its chair from among the members.
(c)	Meetings shall be called by the chair or the city electrical inspector.
(Ord. No. 1982-0005, § 5.51(d)—(f), 5-13-1982) 
Sec. 18-145. - Powers and duties. 
(a)	The board of electrical examiners shall pass on all examinations for licenses covered by this article. 
(b)	The board may modify or waive requirements of this article by a majority of all members in particular cases wherever any rules are shown to involve expense not justified by the protection secured, or for any other reason shown to be impracticable; or whenever it is shown that equivalent or safer construction can be more readily accomplished in other ways; or where an applicant has been licensed by another city. 
(c)	The board shall have such other powers and perform such other duties, including revocation of license and advising with the electrical inspector and the city council, as are necessary for the proper administration of this article or as may be granted or directed by the city council from time to time. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0005, § 5.52, 5-13-1982) 
Sec. 18-146. - Appeals from decision of electrical inspector. 
Any person aggrieved by a decision or ruling of the city electrical inspector shall have the right to appeal to the board of electrical examiners for its review. Such appeal shall be perfected by a request in writing to the city electrical inspector for a hearing, in which writing the nature of the appellant's grievance is briefly described and his correct name and address stated. The chair of the board shall fix a date for the hearing at which the board shall hear the testimony of all parties concerned and shall render a decision within three days after the hearing. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0005, § 5.53(a), 5-13-1982) 
Sec. 18-147. - Bond requirement. 
No license shall be issued until the applicant has furnished to the city secretary an approved bond in the sum of $1,000.00, payable to the city and guaranteeing the faithful performance of all contracts and compliance with all the terms of this article. Such bond shall be liable for all costs incident to or caused by failure of licensee to perform his duties in accordance with the terms of this article. 
(Ord. No. 1982-0005, § 5.54, 5-13-1982) 
Secs. 18-148—18-180. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE IV. - FOOD AND FOOD SERVICE ESTABLISHMENTS 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (6) --- 
Editor's note—Ord. No. 2001-004, §§ 1—26, adopted April 12, 2001, amended article IV in its entirety to read as herein set out. Formerly, article IV pertained to similar subject matter, and derived from Ord. No. 1994-0014, §§ 1, 2(a)—(f), adopted September 13, 1994. 
Sec. 18-181. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meaning ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Applicant means any person seeking a permit to operate a retail food store or food service establishment and every person to whom such a permit has been issued. 
City means the City of Gilmer, Texas. 
Employee means any individual working in a food service establishment or retail food store, whether paid or unpaid, full-time or part-time, on a temporary or permanent basis, or an independent contractor. 
Food means any raw, cooked, or processed edible substance, ice, beverage, or ingredient used or intended for use of for sale in whole or in part for human consumption. 
Food service establishment means any place open to the general public or where, for distinct payment, food and/or drink is prepared or served for human consumption, whether served and consumed on the premises or off the premises. The term includes temporary food service establishments and mobile food units. 
Health department means the health department of the city. 
Health officer means the person designated by the city manager to enforce this article and state law relating to food service establishments and retail food store. 
Mobile food unit means a wheeled or vehicle mounted food service establishment designed to be readily moveable. In addition to the requirements of this article, mobile food units shall comply with additional ordinance requirements of the city. 
Person means any individual, partnership, company, venture, association, trust, estate, foundation, institution, organization, group, governmental subdivision or agency, and any other entity recognized by law as the subject of rights and duties whether operated for profit or not for profit. 
Person in charge means the individual present in a food service establishment or retail food store who is the apparent manager or supervisor of the food service establishment or retail food store at the time of inspection or delivery of notice. If no individual is the apparent supervisor, then any employee present is the person in charge. 
Retail food store means any establishment where the only food offered for sale to ultimate consumers is that which is intended for off-premises consumption. 
Roadside food vendors means a person who operates a mobile food store from a temporary location adjacent to a public roadway or highway. A roadside food vendor is classified herein as a retail food store. 
Temporary food service establishment means a food service establishment that operates at a fixed location for a period of time of not more that 14 consecutive days in conjunction with an event or celebration. 
(Ord. No. 2001-004, § 1, 4-12-2001) 
Sec. 18-182. - Adoption of state rules. 
The laws of the state and the rules of the state department of health governing food service sanitation and retail food store sanitation, as now existing and as may be amended or changed hereafter, are hereby adopted and made a part of this article as if fully set out herein, and the provisions thereof shall govern all matters covered herein within the city. The shall govern all matters covered herein within the city. The provisions of this article are in addition to state laws and rules governing food service sanitation and retail food store sanitation. 
(Ord. No. 2001-004, § 2, 4-12-2001) 
Sec. 18-183. - Permit required. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a food service establishment or retail food store within the city without a valid permit issued to him by the health department of the city. 
(Ord. No. 2001-004, § 3, 4-12-2001) 
Sec. 18-184. - Application for permit. 
Any person desiring to operate a food service establishment or retail food store within the city shall make a written application for such permit on forms to be provided by the city health department. Such application shall, at a minimum, include the following information: 
(1)	The applicant's full name, office address and telephone number, including the address and telephone number of the home office, if any, and whether such applicant is an individual, partnership, corporation or other entity; and, if other that an individual, sufficient information to fully identify the ownership of the applicant. 
(2)	The location and type of food service establishment or retail food store;
(3)	If the application is for a temporary food service establishment, it shall include the inclusive dates of the proposed operation of such establishment; 
(4)	A copy of the applicant's sales tax permit showing its tax location in the city.
(5)	A statement by the applicant that he is not delinquent upon any account owed to the city or otherwise indebted to city, said accounts and indebtedness including, but not limited to, unpaid taxes, garbage collection fees, assessments, fines, and permit and license fees; and 
(6)	The signature of the applicant or applicants.
(Ord. No. 2001-004, § 4, 4-12-2001) 
Sec. 18-185. - Inspection by health department and records access. 
Upon receipt of such application, the health department shall make an inspection of the food service establishment or retail food store to determine compliance with the revisions of this article and state law. The health department may make such inspections thereafter, as it shall deem necessary to ensure compliance with the provisions of this article and state law. The health department shall be permitted to examine the records of the establishment or store to obtain information pertaining to food and supplies. 
(Ord. No. 2001-004, § 5, 4-12-2001) 
Sec. 18-186. - Issuance of permit. 
When inspection by the health department reveals that the applicable requirements of this article and state law have been met, including the payment of a permit fee as required, and finds that the applicant is not delinquent in any amount due to the city, a permit shall be issued to the applicant by the health department. 
(Ord. No. 2001-004, § 6, 4-12-2001) 
Sec. 18-187. - Permit fees. 
The annual permit fee to be paid by each applicant shall be as follows: 
(1)	For each establishment having one and not more than two employees on average, annually .....$ 25.00 
(2)	For each establishment having at least three but not more than five employees on average, annually .....50.00 
(3)	For each establishment having at least six but not more than ten employees on average, annually .....100.00 
(4)	For each establishment having more than ten but not more than 20 employees on average, annually .....125.00 
(5)	For each establishment having more than 20 but not more than 30 employees on average, annually .....150.00 
(6)	For each establishment having more than 30 employees on average, annually .....175.00 
(7)	For each mobile food unit, an annual fee .....100.00 
(8)	For each roadside food vendor, an annual fee .....100.00 
(Ord. No. 2001-004, § 7, 4-12-2001) 
Sec. 18-188. - Record of permit holders and reports. 
Files shall be kept by the health department of the city of all establishments who hold a permit under this article. Said file shall include the permit application, permit copy or receipt, all inspection reports, all other reports, and all other documents related to the operation and requirements of this article. 
(Ord. No. 2001-004, § 8, 4-12-2001) 
Sec. 18-189. - Term and renewal of permit. 
A permit required by this article shall be valid for a period of one year from the date of issuance thereof, unless the same is sooner revoked or suspended as herein provided, or unless the holder of such permit shall change the location of his place business or sells or otherwise disposes of such business or materially changes the character of such business. Upon the expiration of any such permit and within seven days thereafter, a person conducting or operating such business or vehicle shall apply for and secure renewal thereof in the same manner as herein provided. 
(Ord. No. 2001-004, § 9, 4-12-2001) 
Sec. 18-190. - Display of permit. 
Each permit issued under this article shall at all times be kept publicly displayed in a conspicuous place in or about such place of business, premises, or vehicle. 
(Ord. No. 2001-004, § 10, 4-12-2001) 
Sec. 18-191. - Inspection sheets to be kept. 
Inspection sheets prepared by the city health officer on prior inspections must be kept on the premises to be produced upon request of the health officer. 
(Ord. No. 2001-004, § 11, 4-12-2001) 
Sec. 18-192. - Suspension or revocation of permit; hearings.
