(b)	The city will identify the nearest minority business development agency from the regional office directory and forward a copy of all advertisements for bidders to that agency. 
(c)	Businesses located in the county or adjoining counties that provide services applicable to the city's needs under the HOME Program and are listed in the state certified historically underutilized business directory will be contacted. 
(d)	Minority and/or women-owned business enterprises identified in the city and surrounding areas will be placed on a bidders list to receive a copy of all advertisements soliciting the type of services provided by that business. 
(Ord. No. 2000-006, 8-31-2000) 
Sec. 46-153. - Records and reports. 
(a)	The city shall maintain records and statistical data on participation by minority businesses and women-owned businesses. 
(b)	The city shall submit a historically underutilized business report upon completion of each project. 
(Ord. No. 2000-006, 8-31-2000)

ARTICLE II. - POLICE RESERVE FORCE 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (2) --- 
Charter reference— Special police, § 4.04.2 
State Law reference— Police reserve force, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code §§ 141.007, 142.003, 341.012. 
Sec. 50-31. - Created. 
There is created in and for the city a police reserve force in accordance with V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 341.012, such article to be used as a guideline for the creation of the police reserve force and as a guideline for adopting subsequent rules, policies, procedures or other provisions by which the police reserve force shall be governed and regulated. 
(Ord. No. 1980-0008, § 12-16, 7-10-1980) 
Sec. 50-32. - Size. 
The maximum number of members of the police reserve force shall at no time exceed 20 members. 
(Ord. No. 1980-0008, § 12-17, 7-10-1980) 
Sec. 50-33. - Appointment of members. 
(a)	The chief of police shall appoint the members of the reserve force. Members serve at the chief's discretion. 
(b)	Appointments to the reserve force must be approved by the city council before the person appointed may carry a weapon or otherwise act as a peace officer. After the appointment is approved, the person appointed may carry a weapon only when authorized to do so by the chief of police and only when discharging official duties as a peace officer. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 341.012(d), (g).  
Sec. 50-34. - Duties of members. 
(a)	The chief of police may call the reserve force into service at any time the chief considers it necessary to have additional officers to preserve the peace and enforce the law. 
(b)	Members of the reserve force serve as peace officers during the actual discharge of official duties. 
(c)	Reserve police officers may act only in a supplementary capacity to the regular police force and may not assume the full-time duties of regular police officers without complying with the requirements for regular police officers. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 341.012(e), (f), (h).  
Chapter 54 - MISCELLANEOUS OFFENSES 
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Law enforcement, ch. 50; traffic and vehicles, ch. 86  
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 54-1. - Panhandling prohibited. 
(a)	Intent and purpose. It is the purpose of this section to regulate panhandling to promote the health, safety, and general welfare of the residents of the city, and to protect and preserve the quality and character of the city. It is expressly not the intent or effect of this section to impose a limitation upon rights granted under the First Amendment. 
(b)	Definitions. 
Panhandling, for the purposes of this section, is any solicitation made in person requesting an immediate donation of money or thing of value. Panhandling includes the purchase of an item or service under circumstances where a reasonable person would understand that the purchase is in substance a donation. 
(c)	Time of panhandling. Any person who panhandles after sunset or before sunrise is guilty of a class C misdemeanor. 
(d)	Place of panhandling. Any person who panhandles in any public area or any public roadway is guilty of a class C misdemeanor. 
(e)	Manner of panhandling. Any person who panhandles in any of the following manners is guilty of a class C misdemeanor: 
(1)	By blocking the path of the person solicited along a sidewalk or street;
(2)	By following a person who walks away from the panhandler;
(3)	By using profane or abusive language, either during the solicitation or following a refusal; or 
(4)	By any statement, gesture, or other communication which a reasonable person in the situation of the person solicited would perceive to be a threat. 
(f)	Panhandling that is false or misleading. Any person who knowingly makes any false or misleading representation in the course of soliciting a donation is guilty of a class C misdemeanor. False or misleading representations include, but are not limited to, the following: 
(1)	Stating that the solicitor is homeless when he is not;
(2)	Stating that the solicitor is from out of town and stranded when that is not true;
(3)	Using makeup or device to simulate any deformity;
(4)	Wearing or displaying an indication of physical disability when the solicitor does not suffer the disability indicated; 
(5)	Wearing a military uniform or other indication of military service when the solicitor is neither a present nor former member of the service indicated; or 
(6)	Stating that the donation is needed to meet a need which does not exist or the solicitor already has sufficient funds to meet. 
(g)	Authorization for panhandling by pedestrian. Not withstanding the provisions of subsections (d) and (e) and, as authorized by V.T.C.A., Transportation Code (2005), § 552.0071, a person or persons shall be authorized to stand in a roadway to solicit (as that term is used in subsection (a)) a contribution to an organization defined as charitable by the standards of the United States Internal Revenue Service if the person or persons to be engaged in the solicitation are employees or agents of the city. 
(Ord. No. 2006-010, Arts. I—VII, 12-12-2006)
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2006-010, Arts. I—VII, adopted December 12, 2006, did not specify manner of inclusion; hence, inclusion as § 54-1 is at the discretion of the editor.  
Secs. 54-2—54-30. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - WEAPONS 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference— Hunting, use of dangerous weapons on airport property, § 10-104  
Sec. 54-31. - Discharge of firearms. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge any firearm within the city limits; however, this section shall not be construed to prohibit any officer of the law from discharging a firearm in the performance of his duty nor to any citizen from discharging a firearm when lawfully defending person or property. Any person found guilty of such unlawful discharge of a firearm within the city limits shall be fined not more than $200.00. 
(Ord. No. 1984-0018, 8-9-1984) 
Sec. 54-32. - Possession of firearm in city-owned building; exception. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person to carry onto the premises of, or to possess any firearm on the premises of, any building owned by the city. 
(b)	This section shall not apply to any licensed police officer.
(Ord. No. 1996-0001, arts. I, II, 1-25-1996)

ARTICLE III. - MINORS  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Secs. 54-61—54-80. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - CURFEW 
 
Sec. 54-81. - Scope. 
This division establishes curfew hours for minors within the corporate city limits of the city and shall also apply to its extraterritorial jurisdiction. 
(Ord. No. 1996-0011, § 1, 5-9-1996) 
Sec. 54-82. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Chief of police means the chief of police of the city or a designated representative. 
Curfew hours means: 
(1)	10:00 p.m. to 6:00 a.m. any day except Friday or Saturday; and
(2)	12:00 midnight to 6:00 a.m. Friday and Saturday.
Direct route means the shortest path of travel through a public place to reach a final destination without any detour or stop along the way. 
Emergency means but is not limited to a fire, a natural disaster, an automobile accident, or any situation requiring immediate action to prevent serious bodily injury or loss of life. 
Establishment means any privately owned place of business operated for a profit to which the public is invited, including but not limited to any place of amusement or entertainment. 
Holding location means a place designated by the chief of police to which a minor taken into custody for a violation of this division will be delivered to await pickup by a parent or juvenile authorities. 
Minor means any person under 17 years of age. 
Operator means any individual, firm, association, partnership or corporation operating, managing or conducting any establishment. The term "operator" includes the members or partners of an association or partnership and the officers of a corporation. 
Parent means a person who is: 
(1)	A natural or adoptive parent of another person;
(2)	A court-appointed guardian of another person; or
(3)	At least 21 years of age and authorized by a parent or court-appointed guardian to have the care and custody of another person. 
Public place means any street, alley, highway, sidewalk, playground, park, plaza, building or other place used by or open to the public. 
Remain means to: 
(1)	Linger or stay unnecessarily; or
(2)	Fail to leave premises when requested to do so by a police officer or the owner, operator or other person in control of the premises. 
(Ord. No. 1996-0011, § 2(2.01(A)), 5-9-1996)
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2  
Sec. 54-83. - Offenses. 
(a)	A minor commits an offense if he remains in any public place or on the premises of any establishment within the city during curfew hours. 
(b)	A parent of a minor commits an offense if he knowingly permits or by insufficient control allows the minor to remain in any public place or on the premises of any establishment within the city during curfew hours. 
(c)	The owner, operator or any employee of an establishment commits an offense if he knowingly allows a minor to remain upon the premises of the establishment during curfew hours. 
(Ord. No. 1996-0011, § 2(2.01(B)), 5-9-1996) 
Sec. 54-84. - Defenses. 
It is a defense to prosecution under section 54-83 that the minor was: 
(1)	Accompanied by the minor's parent;
(2)	On an errand at the direction of the minor's parent and was using a direct route;
(3)	In a motor vehicle involved in interstate travel;
(4)	Engaged in an employment activity, including but not limited to newspaper delivery, and was using a direct route; 
(5)	Involved in an emergency;
(6)	On the sidewalk abutting the minor's residence or abutting the residence of a next-door neighbor if the neighbor did not complain to the police officer about the minor's presence; 
(7)	Attending an official school or religious activity or returning home by a direct route from an official school or religious activity; 
(8)	Exercising First Amendment rights protected by the United States Constitution, such as the free exercise of religion, freedom of speech and the right of assembly; or 
(9)	Married or had been married or had disabilities of minority removed in accordance with V.T.C.A., Family Code § 31.001 et seq. 
(Ord. No. 1996-0011, § 2(2.01(C)), 5-9-1996) 
Sec. 54-85. - Enforcement. 
(a)	A police officer, upon finding a minor in violation of section 54-83, shall ascertain the name and address of the minor and shall inquire into the reasons for the minor's being in a public place. If the police officer reasonably believes that the minor has violated this division and that no defenses apply, a citation may be issued to the minor; and the police officer may order the minor to go promptly home by a direct route or may take the minor into custody and deliver the minor to a holding location. 
(b)	When a minor is taken into custody under this section, the police department shall immediately notify a parent to pick up the minor at the holding location. After a parent arrives at a holding location and provides the information required by the chief of police to file an incident report, the minor shall be released into the custody of the parent. If a parent cannot be located or fails to take charge of the minor, the police officer shall contact a police department juvenile officer. 
(c)	If a minor is not taken into custody for a violation of section 54-83, the police department shall notify a parent of the minor that the minor has violated section 54-83 and may issue a citation to the minor's parent if reasonable grounds exist to believe that the parent has violated section 54-83 
(d)	A police officer shall, after finding a minor in violation of section 54-83, file a written report on the incident. 
(Ord. No. 1996-0011, § 2(2.01(D)), 5-9-1996) 
Sec. 54-86. - Penalties. 
(a)	A minor may be prosecuted in municipal court for a violation of section 54-83(a). An individual adjudged guilty of a violation of section 54-83(a) shall be punished by a fine not to exceed $500.00. 
(b)	A parent of a minor who violates section 54-83(b) may be prosecuted in municipal court. An individual adjudged guilty of violation of section 54-83(b) shall be punished by a fine not to exceed $500.00. 
(c)	The owner, operator or employee of an establishment who violates section 54-83(c) may be prosecuted in municipal court. An individual adjudged guilty of violation of section 54-83(c) shall be punished by a fine not to exceed $500.00. 
(d)	Any minor who violates section 54-83(a) three or more times within a 24-month period is subject to appropriate action by a juvenile court in accordance with V.T.C.A., Family Code chs. 51 and 52. 
(Ord. No. 1996-0011, § 2(2.01(E)), 5-9-1996)  
Chapter 58 - MUNICIPAL COURT 
FOOTNOTE(S):

ARTICLE II. - FUNDS  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY

DIVISION 2. - BUILDING SECURITY FUND 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Building security fund, Vernon's Ann. C.C.P. art. 102.017. 
Sec. 58-51. - Created. 
There is created a city municipal court building security fund. 
(Ord. No. 1998-0014, § 3, 2-10-1998) 
Sec. 58-52. - Security fee. 
There shall be and is hereby assessed a security fee on file in the city secretary's office as a cost of court to be assessed for the purposes of funding the city municipal court building security fund created in this division. Each defendant charged and convicted of a misdemeanor offense in the municipal court (unless exempted in this division) is directed to and shall pay the security fee as a cost of court. For purposes of this section, a person is considered convicted, whether upon a finding of guilt in open court, or by plea of guilt or nolo contendere (by mail or otherwise), or by payment of fine for a moving traffic violation or other violation punishable by a fine only (thereby constituting a finding of guilt in open court and a plea of nolo contendere), if: 
(1)	A sentence is imposed on the person;
(2)	The person receives community supervision, including deferred adjudication; or
(3)	The court defers final disposition of the person's case.
(Ord. No. 1998-0014, § 6, 2-10-1998) 
Sec. 58-53. - Collection; expenditures. 
The clerk of the municipal court shall collect the costs authorized in this division and forward them for deposit to the city treasury, to the credit of the municipal court building security fund. Thereafter, expenditures shall be made from that fund for the purposes authorized in this division in accordance with the directives of the city council. 
(Ord. No. 1998-0014, § 7, 2-10-1998) 
Sec. 58-54. - Use. 
The moneys deposited in the municipal court building security fund shall be used exclusively to finance the following items when used for the purpose of providing security services for buildings housing the municipal court, as appropriate: 
(1)	The purchase or repair of X-ray machines and conveying systems;
(2)	Hand-held metal detectors;
(3)	Walk-through metal detectors;
(4)	Identification cards and systems;
(5)	Electronic locking and surveillance equipment;
(6)	Bailiffs or other contract security personnel during times when they are providing appropriate security services; 
(7)	Signage;
(8)	Confiscated weapon inventory and tracking systems;
(9)	Locks, chains or other security hardware; or
(10)	Continuing education on security issues for court personnel and security personnel.
(Ord. No. 1998-0014, § 4, 2-10-1998) 
Sec. 58-55. - Administration. 
The municipal court building security fund shall be administered by or under the direction of the city council. 
(Ord. No. 1998-0014, § 5, 2-10-1998)
Cross reference— Administration, ch. 2  
Secs. 58-56—58-80. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 3. - TECHNOLOGY FUND 
 
Sec. 58-81. - Created. 
There is created a municipal court technology fund. 
(Ord. No. 2000-007, 9-14-2000) 
Sec. 58-82. - Technology fee. 
(a)	A defendant convicted of a misdemeanor offense in municipal court shall pay a $4.00 technology fee as a cost of court. 
(b)	For purpose of this section, a person is considered convicted if:
(1)	A sentence is imposed on the person;
(2)	The person is placed on community supervision, including deferred adjudication; or
(3)	The court defers final disposition of the defendant's case.
(Ord. No. 2000-007, 9-14-2000) 
Sec. 58-83. - Collection; expenditures. 
(a)	The municipal court clerk shall collect the costs and pay the funds to the city financial director for the deposit in the municipal court technology fund. 
(b)	The municipal court technology fund may be used only to finance the purchase of technological enhancements for the municipal court, including: 
(1)	Computer systems;
(2)	Computer networks;
(3)	Computer hardware;
(4)	Computer software;
(5)	Imaging system;
(6)	Electronic Kiosks;
(7)	Electronic ticket writers; and
(8)	Docket management systems.
(Ord. No. 2000-007, 9-14-2000) 
Sec. 58-84. - Administration. 
The municipal court technology fund shall be administered by the city manager under the direction of the city council. 
(Ord. No. 2000-007, 9-14-2000)

Sec. 62-1. - Possession or consumption of alcoholic beverages in public parks prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to possess or consume any alcoholic beverages in any public park within the city limits.

DIVISION 2. - PARK ADVISORY BOARD 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (3) --- 
Cross reference— Board, committees, commissions, § 2-31 et seq. 
Sec. 62-51. - Created, established; officers. 
(a)	There is created and established within the city a park advisory board that shall be composed of seven members to be appointed by the city council for three-year overlapping terms. Appointments shall be made at the first meeting in January of each year. In making the initial appointments, the council shall designate which terms shall expire in January 1999 and January 2001. 
(b)	The board shall select from among its members the chair, vice-chair and secretary and copies of the minutes of all meetings shall be delivered to the city manager. The chair will be responsible for calling all meetings and notifying the city of the time and date in case of conflicting interests. 
(Ord. No. 1998-0002, 3-26-1998) 
Sec. 62-52. - Duties and recommendations. 
The park advisory board shall set up guidelines for the use, equipment, acquisition or lease of any part of park property and expenditure of funds. These guidelines shall be set out in writing and copies made available to the city manager and the city council, who shall review the guidelines and have the authority to make any changes or additions in the guidelines. 
(Ord. No. 1998-0002, 3-26-1998) 
Sec. 62-53. - Authority. 
All authority vested by this Code of Ordinances to parks and public recreation areas is vested in the park advisory board.  
Secs. 62-54—62-80. - Reserved.

DIVISION 2. - ABNEY PARK 
 
Sec. 62-101. - Hours open to the public. 
The Abney Street Park shall open to the public at 6:00 a.m., seven days per week, and shall be closed to the public at 12:00 midnight on Sunday, Monday, Tuesday, Wednesday, and Thursday nights. On Friday and Saturday nights, the Abney Street Park shall close to the public at 1:00 a.m.

ARTICLE IV. - LAKE GILMER 
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (4) --- 
Editor's note—Ord. No. 2001-011, adopted September 27, 2001, enacted provisions intended for use as article IV, §§ 63.1—63.17, 63.26—63.37, 63.46, 63.51, 63.53, 63.54, 63.61, 63.66, and 63.67. To preserve the style of this Code, and at the discretion of the editor, said provisions have been redesignated as §§ 62-131—62-146, 62-161, 62-171—62-181, 62-191, 62-201—62-203, 62-211, 62-221, and 62-231  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Sec. 62-131. - Area of authority. 
This article applies to all waters impounded by dams constituting Lake Gilmer and its tributaries and the adjacent lands owned or controlled by the city, herein referred to as the lake. Certain area adjacent to the lake have been set aside for development by the city as public parks and picnic areas. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-132. - Authority of peace officers on reservoir property. 
Any peace officer certified as marine safety enforcement officer shall have authority to arrest any person on the lake for any violation of this article, and/or to exclude any person found violating this article from the lake. Any peace officer shall have authority to arrest any person on flood pool or mitigation property. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-133. - Responsibility powers and duties of city. 
The city shall have full charge and control of the waters of the reservoirs and grounds of the lake. The Gilmer Lake Rangers shall keep the peace and patrol the lake in order to enforce this article and all other laws, ordinances, rules and regulations of the city/state relating to the waters of the lake and to make arrests for any violation of this article or other city ordinances and state laws. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-134. - Outlet works and spillways. 
No watercraft, swimming, or fishing is allowed within 100 feet of the mouth of the spillway. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-135. - Dam. 
It is unlawful to operate any motorized vehicle upon the dam on the lake. Foot traffic and fishing are not permitted on the dam. It is unlawful for any person to throw fish line in the rock rip-rapped area. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-136. - Raw water intake. 
It is unlawful for any person except authorized repair or maintenance personnel to approach within a 100-foot radius of the water intake for any reason. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-137. - Camping. 
(a)	Camping on city-owned property is permitted in designated park areas only.
(b)	Camp equipment shall not be abandoned or left unattended for a period of more than 24 hours. 
(c)	No person will be allowed to camp on city-owned property for any one period of one week or longer. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001)
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2001-011, adopted September 27, 2001, enacted provisions intended for use as subsections 1.—3. To preserve the style of this Code, and at the discretion of the editor, said provisions have been redesignated as subsections (a)—(c).  
Sec. 62-138. - Diving from structures. 
It is unlawful for any person to dive from or off of any structure or part of any public bridge or an appurtenance thereto. This prohibition as to diving also includes using rope, cable, or other apparatus attached to a bridge or other structure or object, including a tree, so as to permit an individual to swing out over the waters of the lake. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-139. - Parking of motor vehicles. 
It is unlawful for any person to leave unattended any motor vehicle with a boat trailer in tow in any designated safety or turn around zone except as necessary while loading or unloading a boat. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-140. - Damaging signs, markers and buoys. 
It is unlawful for any person to deface, destroy or otherwise damage any sign marker or buoys, placed by the city on the lake. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-141. - Livestock and fowl prohibited. 
It is unlawful for any person to keep or harbor any livestock or fowl on city property at the lake. No livestock is allowed in or upon public parks, boat ramps, beaches, designated picnic areas, the dam, or spillway. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-142. - Cutting trees or brush, disturbing sodding. 
(a)	Trees/brush. It is unlawful for any person to cut any trees or brush on any city-owned property at the lake without the approval of the lake manager. 
(b)	Sodding. Sodding may not be disturbed unnecessarily. Soil may not be removed nor the natural contour disturbed in any way on city owned property. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001)
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2001-011, adopted September 27, 2001, enacted provisions intended for use as subsections 1. and 2. To preserve the style of this Code, and at the discretion of the editor, said provisions have been redesignated as subsections (a) and (b).  
Sec. 62-143. - Dumping of garbage, brush, and trash. 
It is unlawful for any person to dump trash, brush, or garbage of any kind except in places designated by the city. Trash receptacles located in parks, on beaches, and at boat ramps are for facility users only, and no household garbage may be deposited in these containers. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-144. - USACE Permit #199100466. 
These rules and regulations of the city are specifically enacted to comply with terms and conditions of United Corp of Engineers Permit #199100466. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-145. - Flotation devices. 
It is unlawful for any person to place barrels, or other such containers upon, or in the waters of the lake. The city may employ such devices for markers or other similar uses. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-146. - Possession or consumption of alcoholic beverages on Lake Gilmer. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to possess or consume any alcoholic beverage on Lake Gilmer. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Secs. 62-147—62-160. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - DEFINITIONS 
 
Sec. 62-161. - Definitions. 
For the purpose of this article, the following definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning: 
Boat means any watercraft, other than a seaplane on water, used or capable of being used for transportation on water. 
Gilmer Lake rangers means the law enforcement agency commissioned by TCLEOSE, to preserve order within the lake and mitigation and other properties, as noted. 
Lake Gilmer or lake means the lake located in the city, upshur County Texas, created by the construction of the dam on Kelsey Creek by the city and all mitigation and other properties, as noted. 
Motorboat means any watercraft propelled by machinery, whether or not the machinery is the principal source of propulsion. 
Operate means to navigate or otherwise use a boat. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Secs. 62-162—62-170. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 3. - BOATS AND BOATING REGULATIONS 
 
Sec. 62-171. - Boating regulations. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person operating a boat with toilet accommodations to discharge waste materials from the boat's toilet into the waters of Lake Gilmer. 
(b)	No person may operate any boat at a rate of speed greater than is reasonable and prudent, having due regard for the conditions and hazards, actual and potential, then existing, including weather and density of traffic, or greater than will permit him, in the exercise of reasonable care, to bring the boat to a stop within the assured clear distance ahead, In the boat docking area or inside the "no-wake" area, the operator of a boat shall control the speed of said boat as may be necessary to prevent the leaving of a wake behind said boat. 
(c)	No person may operate a boat propelled in whole or in part by a motor fueled by gas, gasoline, diesel, or naphtha, unless the same is equipped with a muffler, underwater exhaust, or other device capable of adequately muffling the sound of the motor's exhaust. "Adequately muffling" shall mean that the motor's exhaust is at all times so muffled or suppressed as not to create excessive or unusual noise. 
(d)	No motorboat larger than a motorboat classified as "class 2" by V.T.C.A., Parks and Wildlife Code § 31.026 may be operated on Lake Gilmer (less than 26 feet). 
(e)	Water skiing and personal watercraft will only be allowed on the area east of the Highway 852 bridge. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001)
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2001-011, adopted September 27, 2001, enacted provisions intended for use as subsections 1.—5. To preserve the style of this Code, and at the discretion of the editor, said provisions have been redesignated as subsections (a)—(e).  
Sec. 62-172. - Safe operation of boats; tow boat clearance of vessels. 
Boats towing disabled craft have the right-of-way. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-173. - Anchoring of barges or boats at pier, buoys, etc. 
Except for emergencies it is unlawful for any person to cause or permit any boat, barge or other watercraft to anchor or tie up at any public pier for more than one hour. It is unlawful for any boat, barge or other watercraft to anchor or tie up at any posted sign, buoy, or other marker on the waters of the lake or its tributaries except in case of emergency. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-174. - Unattended boats. 
It is unlawful for any person to leave a boat, barge, or other watercraft unattended on the waters of the lake, except in cases of emergency. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-175. - Obstruction of ramps. 
It is unlawful for any person to block any public boat loading ramp leading to the waters of the lake. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-176. - Removal of unsafe craft from lake. 
The city may require the removal of any boat or other craft from the lake if it is deemed a navigational hazard or is in an unsafe operating condition. In the event of noncompliance by the owner to such order, the craft will be removed from the lake by the city and the owner will be assessed all costs. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-177. - Overloading. 
No person owning or operating a boat, barge, or other watercraft on the lake may permit it to be occupied by more persons than the rated capacity of such boat or other craft, or to be loaded with passengers or cargo beyond its safe capacity, taking into consideration weather and other operating conditions. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-178. - Passengers to be seated in motorboats. 
(a)	No person operating a motorboat on the lake may allow any person to ride or sit on the gunwales (side rails) thereof or on the decking over the bow of the craft while underway, nor allow any person to stand in such craft while underway. This provision does not apply to the operator of barges or similar craft on which no operator seat is provided. 
(b)	Passengers or other persons aboard a motorboat may stand in the decking over the bow of the boat to moor the boat or to cast of or for nay other necessary purpose. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001)
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2001-011, adopted September 27, 2001, enacted provisions intended for use as subsections 1. and 2. To preserve the style of this Code, and at the discretion of the editor, said provisions have been redesignated as subsections (a) and (b).  
Sec. 62-179. - Toilets. 
It is unlawful for any person to place or maintain a toilet on any boat or barge except unattached, portable, chemical toilets. Such toilet must be approved and certified by a lake ranger before being taken aboard the craft. All boats, barges, and other watercraft operated on the lake having enclosures large enough to accommodate a toilet are subject to inspections by the lake ranger. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-180. - Abandoned boats, barges and watercrafts. 
(a)	Any boat, barge, or watercraft which is found upon the waters of the lake or upon any public property immediately adjacent thereto and which is inoperable and more than five years old and left unattended for more than 48 hours, is deemed to be an abandoned watercraft. For purposed of this section, "watercraft" shall include any motorboat, outboard motor, or vessel subject to registration under state law. 
(b)	The lake manager may authorize taking into custody any abandoned watercraft found upon the waters of, or on any public property immediately adjacent to the lake. Any watercraft deemed a navigational hazard may be removed from the lake. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001)
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2001-011, adopted September 27, 2001, enacted provisions intended for use as subsections 1. and 2. To preserve the style of this Code, and at the discretion of the editor, said provisions have been redesignated as subsections (a) and (b).  
Sec. 62-181. - Texas Parks and Wildlife Code Chapter 31 adopted. 
V.T.C.A., Parks and Wildlife Code ch. 31 concerning boating safety is hereby adopted and incorporated by reference as if fully set out herein. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Secs. 62-182—62-190. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 4. - SWIMMING REGULATIONS 
 
Sec. 62-191. - Swimming regulations. 
(a)	No person may swim in any public launch or docking area of Lake Gilmer. Swimming will not be allowed in the area under the bridge or in area marked by buoys. 
(b)	Swimming within Lake Gilmer, even in areas marked as being available for public swimming, shall be at the risk of the swimmer. 
(c)	It is unlawful for glass containers to be used at the designated swim area.
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001)
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2001-011, adopted September 27, 2001, enacted provisions intended for use as subsections 1.—3. To preserve the style of this Code, and at the discretion of the editor, said provisions have been redesignated as subsections (a)—(c).  
Secs. 62-192—62-200. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 5. - FISHING 
 
Sec. 62-201. - Fishing regulations. 
(a)	No person shall fish within 100 feet of the city intake tower.
(b)	There shall be no closed season or period of time when it shall be unlawful to take, catch or retain freshwater fish by the use of ordinary hook and line or artificial lure. 
(c)	V.T.C.A., Parks and Wildlife Code ch. 66, concerning fishing, as well as the rules and regulations of the parks and wildlife department are hereby adopted and incorporated by reference as if fully set out herein. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001)
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2001-011, adopted September 27, 2001, enacted provisions intended for use as subsections 1.—3. To preserve the style of this Code, and at the discretion of the editor, said provisions have been redesignated as subsections (a)—(c).  
Sec. 62-202. - Prohibited in swimming area. 
It is unlawful for any person to fish, or set out trotlines, gang hooks or fish nets in any area or portion thereof of the waters of the lake that has been restricted for swimming. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Sec. 62-203. - Use of metal line, cable prohibited. 
It is unlawful for any person to place or extend any metal line or cable in, over, on, or across the waters of the lake. This provision shall not apply to any fishing line or fishing device. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Secs. 62-204—62-210. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 6. - WEAPONS, HUNTING PROHIBITED 
 
Sec. 62-211. - Discharging of weapons, hunting prohibited. 
(a)	It is unlawful for a person to shoot, discharge, or hunt with a bow, crossbow, slingshot, gun, firearm, or any other type of weapon in, on, over, across, or upon the mitigation land of Lake Gilmer. 
(b)	No hunting is allowed on the area of the lake that is east of the Highway 852 bridge. Hunting for waterfowl from a boat, barge, or watercraft will be allowed on the area of the lake west of the Highway 852 bridge. 
(c)	It is unlawful for a person to discharge a firearm on city property. However, it shall be lawful for a person to possess and discharge a firearm on the area of the lake west of the Highway 852 bridge as long as the possession and discharge are as part of a lawful activity. It shall also be lawful to possess a firearm from the area of the city boat dock to the area of the Highway 852 bridge if the purpose of such possession of said firearm is to lawfully hunt on the area of Lake Gilmer west of Highway 852 bridge. 
(d)	Non-applicability. V.T.C.A, Penal Code § 46.15(a)(1) peace officer.
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001)
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2001-011, adopted September 27, 2001, enacted provisions intended for use as subsections 1.—4. To preserve the style of this Code, and at the discretion of the editor, said provisions have been redesignated as subsections (a)—(d).  
Secs. 62-212—62-220. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 7. - WATER SAFETY 
 
Sec. 62-221. - Compliance with state statutes. 
These rules and regulations of the city are specifically enacted to comply with the terms and conditions of V.T.C.A., Water Safety Act ch. 31, as adopted by 77th Regular Legislative Session. 
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001) 
Secs. 62-222—62-230. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 8. - SCHEDULE OF FINES AND FEES 
 
Sec. 62-231. - Fines and fees. 
(a)	Any person violating any provision of this article shall be guilty of a class C misdemeanor not to exceed $500.00 in municipal court unless otherwise specified by state law. 
(b)	Fees for reclaiming a derelict boat or barge.
(1)	Fees for reclaiming derelict boat: $50.00.
(2)	Fees for reclaiming derelict barge: $100.00.
(Ord. No. 2001-011, 9-27-2001)
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2001-011, adopted September 27, 2001, enacted provisions intended for use as subsections 1. and 2. To preserve the style of this Code, and at the discretion of the editor, said provisions have been redesignated as subsections (a) and (b).

ARTICLE II. - GARAGE SALES 
 
Sec. 66-31. - Limited. 
(a)	Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Garage sale and yard sale mean the temporary retail use of residentially zoned property consisting of the sale of four or more items acquired by the seller for his ultimate use or consumption. 
(b)	Number limited. No person or family shall conduct garage or yard sales for more than four consecutive calendar days. No person or family shall conduct more than three garage or yard sales in any 12-month period. 
(Ord. No. 1995-0011, § 1, 6-8-1995) 
Chapter 70 - SIGNS 
FOOTNOTE(S):

Secs. 70-31—70-50. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - PERMITS 
 
Sec. 70-51. - Required; installation; charge. 
(a)	Sign permits shall be required for all detached signs exceeding 40 square feet in area. 
(b)	All detached signs exceeding 50 square feet in area must be installed or erected by a licensed and bonded sign contractor after obtaining a sign permit from the city. 
(c)	The charge for sign permits shall be on file in the city secretary's office.
(Ord. No. 1999-002, § 3(X), 2-25-1999) 
Secs. 70-52—70-80. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - REGULATIONS  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Sec. 70-81. - General sign requirements. 
This section shall apply to any type of sign within any district: 
(1)	Signs that contain, include or are illuminated by any flashing intermittent or moving lights or intermittent message of any nature are prohibited on interstate, state, federal and primary highways, except those giving only public service information such as time, date, temperature, weather or similar information. 
(2)	No sign shall be so illuminated that it interferes with the effectiveness of, or obscures, an official traffic sign, device or signal. 
(3)	Signs shall be located at least ten feet from any street, except signs for shopping centers and shopping malls and billboards shall be at least 25 feet from any street. 
(4)	Attached signs shall not exceed the height of the wall of the building.
(5)	Signs shall not be located in or permitted to project into public rights-of-way.
(6)	When any sign is illuminated, the lights shall be directed, shaded or concealed so that they will not interfere with the vision of motor vehicle operators or shine directly on residential property. 
(7)	Detached signs shall comply with the following height restrictions:
a.	The top of detached signs in R-1, R-2, RM-1 and RM-2 shall not exceed a maximum height of ten feet nor exceed a maximum height of 35 feet. 
b.	The top of detached signs in MF-1 and MF-2 districts shall not exceed a maximum of 35 feet. 
c.	The top of detached signs in B-1, B-2, L-1 and G-1 shall not exceed a maximum height of 50 feet. 
d.	In shopping centers or malls containing ten acres or more, detached signs may be erected up to a maximum height of 75 feet, provided that such detached signs erected at a height greater than 50 feet must be set back from all property lines a minimum distance equal to the height of the sign. 
e.	The top of billboards shall not exceed a maximum height of 35 feet.
f.	Signs projecting from a building or extending over public property shall maintain a clear height of 9½ feet above the sidewalk, and all such signs shall extend not more than within 18 inches of the curbline. 
(8)	Roof-mounted signs shall be permitted provided they comply with all applicable requirements of the city's building code, chapter 14 
(9)	No sign shall be attached to any trees, utility poles or trash receptacles.
(10)	Signs may not be located in such a manner as to obscure or otherwise interfere with the driver's view of approaching, merging or intersecting traffic or with the effectiveness of an official traffic sign or signal device. 
(11)	All signs shall be kept in good repair and repainted as needed. If a sign becomes unsightly and the owner refuses to repair or repaint within 60 days of notice by the city, the city will contract to have the sign repaired and/or repainted and bill the owner for the contract cost. 
(12)	All signs shall be maintained in good appearance and safe structural condition. The general area in the vicinity of any sign shall be kept free and clear of weeds, debris, trash and litter. 
(13)	All illuminated signs shall be installed and wired in accordance with the requirements of the current National Electrical Code. 
(14)	No sign shall be erected or installed closer than five feet to any telecommunications or television cable, power line or streetlight standard. 
(15)	Should any sign become insecure, in danger of falling or otherwise unsafe, the building official shall provide the owner or the person or firm maintaining the sign, ten days' written notice to secure the sign in a manner approved by the building official or to remove the sign. If action to secure and/or remove such sign is not taken within ten days of such notice, the building official may remove such sign at the expense of the owner or the person or firm maintaining the sign. 
(Ord. No. 1999-002, § 3(IX), 2-25-1999) 
Secs. 70-82—70-100. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - TYPE OF SIGN 
 
Sec. 70-101. - Off-site signs. 
Off-site signs shall be subject to the following restrictions: 
(1)	No more than one sign located off the premises of an establishment shall be permitted on any lot, vacant or occupied. 
(2)	Off-site signs shall not exceed 40 square feet in area.
(Ord. No. 1999-002, § 3(IV), 2-25-1999) 
Sec. 70-102. - Billboards. 
For the purposes of this division, any single detached sign exceeding 250 square feet in gross area and used as an outdoor display for the purpose of making known, advertising or displaying anything shall be determined to be a billboard and shall conform to the following requirements: 
(1)	Billboards shall be allowed only in B-1, B-2 and L-1 districts.
(2)	Billboards shall not be above 35 feet from ground level.
(3)	Billboards shall not exceed 672 square feet in gross area. Billboards that exceed 336 square feet in gross area shall not be stacked or side-by-side. 
(4)	Billboards shall not be erected closer than 300 feet apart on the same side of the street. 
(5)	Billboards may not be located closer than 25 feet to any street.
(6)	Billboards may not be located within 500 feet of any public park, public forest or recreational area, public playground, public school or scenic area designated as such by the city or any other governmental agency. 
(7)	Within cutouts or enclosed open spaces, 80 percent of the area shall be included in calculating the surface area of a billboard. 
(Ord. No. 1999-002, § 3(V), 2-25-1999) 
Sec. 70-103. - Temporary and/or portable signs. 
Temporary and/or portable signs within all districts shall be subject to the following requirements: 
(1)	Real estate signs pertaining to the lease, hire or sale of real estate shall not exceed 40 square feet in area and shall be located on the lot so advertised provided there is only one sign on each street fronting the property. 
(2)	Construction signs pertaining to the construction or remodeling of a building on the premises shall not exceed 60 square feet in area and shall be located on the lot only for the duration of the construction. No more than one sign shall be permitted on each street fronting the property. 
(3)	Development signs pertaining to residential, office, commercial and industrial development shall not exceed 100 square feet in area and shall be located within the area being developed. No more than one sign shall be permitted on each street fronting the property. 
(4)	Temporary and/or portable signs that contain, include or are illuminated by flashing, intermittent or moving lights are prohibited in all nonbusiness districts or state and federal highways. 
(5)	Temporary and/or portable signs that are illuminated by nonintermittent lighting shall be allowed in the following districts: B-1, B-2, L-1 and G-1. Temporary and/or portable signs located in all other districts shall not be illuminated. 
(Ord. No. 1999-002, § 3(VI), 2-25-1999) 
Sec. 70-104. - Political signs. 
For the purposes of this division, any detached sign designed to promote the support of a candidate for elected office or to promote a particular viewpoint on a matter or issue to be voted upon by the public shall be determined to be a political sign and shall be subject to the following requirements: 
(1)	Political signs shall not exceed 40 square feet in area.
(2)	Political signs shall not be located in or permitted to project into public rights-of-way and shall be located at least ten feet from any street. 
(3)	Political signs shall not be attached to any trees, utility poles or trash receptacles.
(4)	Political signs shall not be placed, located or erected in any public park, public forest or recreational area, public playground and/or on any property owned by the city. 
(5)	Political signs shall be removed within ten days after the primary, runoff or general election to which the signs pertain, or after the termination of candidacy, whichever occurs first. 
(6)	Political signs that contain, include or are illuminated by flashing, intermittent or moving lights are prohibited in all districts. 
(7)	Political signs that are illuminated by nonintermittent lighting shall be allowed only in the following districts: B-1, B-2, L-1 and G-1. Political signs located in all other districts shall not be illuminated. 
(8)	Political signs placed, located or erected in violation of this division shall be subject to immediate removal, confiscation and disposal by city personnel. 
(Ord. No. 1999-002, § 3(VII), 2-25-1999) 
Sec. 70-105. - Garage sale signs. 
Signs for garage sales shall be limited to the following requirements: 
(1)	Only one sign shall be allowed for each garage sale, and that sign shall be located on the same property where the garage sale is located. 
(2)	Garage sale signs shall not be illuminated.
(3)	Signs for garage sales shall not exceed 12 square feet in area.
(4)	Garage sale signs shall be removed within 24 hours after the garage sale has concluded.
(Ord. No. 1999-002, § 3(VIII), 2-25-1999) 
Secs. 70-106—70-130. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 3. - MAIN STREET HISTORIC AREA 
 
Sec. 70-131. - Scope. 
This division only applies to signs located in the Gilmer Main Street Designated Area. In historic areas the character of a street is established as much by the elements attached to the buildings as by the structures themselves. Section 70-137 illustrates the Proper Signage for Gilmer Main Street Historic Buildings. 
(Ord. No. 1999-002, § 2, 2-25-1999) 
Sec. 70-132. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Awning sign means any sign painted or applied to the face, valance or side panels of an awning. 
Hanging sign means any sign suspended from an awning or canopy. 
Pedestrian sign means any sign oriented to pedestrian or street level visibility (including window signs, nameplates and plaques). 
Projecting sign means any sign attached to and placed perpendicular to a building facade. 
Signboard means any flat sign mounted or applied to a building facade. 
Window sign means any sign painted or applied to window glass. 
(Ord. No. 1999-002, § 2(I), 2-25-1999)
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2  
Sec. 70-133. - Number of signs. 
(a)	Each building may have one signboard, awning sign or projecting sign oriented to its primary or entrance facade. 
(b)	A building located at a corner may also have one signboard oriented to its secondary or side street frontage. 
(c)	In addition to a signboard, projecting sign or awning face sign, a building may have one pedestrian sign oriented to each street on which the premises have frontage relating to each occupancy within the building or commodities sold in the building. 
(d)	Buildings with public rear entrances may also have one pedestrian sign oriented to the rear of the building relating to each occupancy within the building. 
(e)	Temporary signs and/or banners shall not be continuously displayed for more than 21 calendar days or for more than 100 calendar days per year. 
(Ord. No. 1999-002, § 2(II), 2-25-1999) 
Sec. 70-134. - Location of signs. 
(a)	No sign shall be allowed above the second story windows of a building.
(b)	Awning signs shall be allowed when such signs are painted or applied flat against the awning surface. 
(c)	Hanging signs shall be allowed when such signs have a minimum clearance of seven feet from the sidewalk and do not extend beyond the awning or canopy projection. 
(d)	Projecting signs shall have a minimum clearance from the sidewalk of 9½ feet.
(Ord. No. 1999-002, § 2(III), 2-25-1999) 
Sec. 70-135. - Size of signs. 
(a)	Signboard maximum size shall be based on the following:
(1)	For every one linear foot of building primary or entrance footage, two square feet of sign area shall be allowed. 
(2)	Signboards on secondary or side street frontage shall not extend the size of signboards on the primary or entrance frontage. 
(b)	Window signs shall cover no more than 30 percent of the total glass areas of the window on which they are placed. The sign coverage shall be determined by an imaginary square or rectangle that encompasses the window sign graphics. 
(c)	Each face of a hanging sign shall be no more than eight square feet in size.
(d)	Awning sign size shall not exceed the surface of the awning.
(e)	Projecting signs shall be no more than 15 square feet in size, with a maximum sign height of three feet and shall not project more than 60 inches or half of the sidewalk width, whichever is less. 
(Ord. No. 1999-002, § 2(IV), 2-25-1999) 
Sec. 70-136. - Sign approval and permits. 
(a)	Permits shall be required for all signboard, awning or projecting signs to be installed in the designated Main Street Area. 
(b)	The Main Street director or his designated representative will review signs for compliance with this division. 
(Ord. No. 1999-002, § 2(V), 2-25-1999) 
Sec. 70-137. - Proper signage for Gilmer Main Street historic buildings. 
(a)	The following subsections of this section is an excerpt from Neighborhood Commercial District Design Guidelines, published by the Landmark Preservation Council of Illinois, written by Wallace Rappe, AIA, and edited by Emily J. Harris. Many of these suggestions can apply to Gilmer Main Street. 
(b)	Oversized, projecting and crowded signs compete with each other and produce confusion. Guide all signage decisions by remembering that the building itself is the best sign. A sensitively rehabilitated, well-maintained building is the best advertisement for a business's attention to detail and the quality of its products and services. The following ground rules for signage will create positive images for individual businesses, enhance the visual harmony of the shopping district, and create an environment that attracts customers. They may also dramatically cut signage costs. 
(1)	Use flat signs in consistent places. Place signs on the buildings sign frieze, which is the horizontal flat bank above the store windows. Original signs, either on flat signboards or made of individual letters attached to the sign frieze, were designed as an integral part of the building. Limit signs on other areas of the building. 
(2)	Remove most projecting signs. Signs that hang over the sidewalk can be counterproductive to business because they often obscure individual buildings and interrupt the visual harmony of the street. If projecting signs are to be used, it is essential that they be small in scale and that they be coordinated with surrounding buildings and signs. 
(3)	Limit the information on signs. The shortest message on a sign has the most impact on pedestrians. The name of the business and the street number are essential. Symbols or cutouts of familiar objects, such as a pharmacist's mortar and pestle, can communicate a great deal of information without lettering at all. 
(4)	Limit the size of the sign. Do not allow signs to conceal any of the building's ornamental or architectural features. Adjust the size of the message to the distance that the shopper is from the store. 
(5)	Use materials and colors that are compatible with the building and the streetscape. The simple signs that were originally used on these buildings serve as the best example for new signs. Individual letters made of wood, metal or some types of plastic that can be mounted directly on the frieze are always appropriate. The number of colors used should be limited. Contrasting the lettering with its background is more important for legibility than using bright colors. 
(6)	Use lighting judiciously. While flashing signs or moving signs should be avoided, lighted signs do identify businesses at night and can encourage evening window-shopping. 
(7)	Preserve original and historic signs. Many older buildings display the names of their original owners on the upper part of the building or above doorways at the street level. These should be preserved as part of the neighborhood's history and character. 
(Ord. No. 1999-002, app. A, 2-25-1999) 
Secs. 70-138—70-160. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 4. - OTHER SPECIFIC AREAS 
 
Sec. 70-161. - Scope. 
The regulations set forth in this division qualify or supplement, as the case may be, the district regulations appearing elsewhere in this article. For the purposes of this division, the term "sign" shall refer to both single-faced and double-faced signs, calculated on the basis of only one face of the sign. 
(Ord. No. 1999-002, § 3, 2-25-1999) 
Sec. 70-162. - Signs within R-1, R-2, MF-1, MF-2, RM-1 and RM-2 districts. 
Signs in the R-1, R-2, MF-1, MF-2, RM-1 and RM-2 districts shall be limited to the following: 
(1)	One-family and two-family dwelling units are limited to a nameplate of four square feet. 
(2)	One attached owner-identification sign shall be permitted for each thoroughfare when more than one thoroughfare abuts the property. 
(3)	One detached owner-identification sign shall be permitted for each thoroughfare when more than one thoroughfare abuts the property. 
(4)	Detached signs shall not exceed 40 square feet in area.
(5)	Signs for bed and breakfast or similar home occupations shall not exceed four square feet and shall comply to all city zoning regulations as described by section 16-7, home occupations of appendix A, zoning, with the exception of IV-C. 
(Ord. No. 1999-002, § 3(I), 2-25-1999)
Cross reference— Zoning, app. A.  
Sec. 70-163. - Signs within B-1, B-2, L-1 and G-1 districts. 
Signs in the B-1, B-2, L-1 and G-1 districts shall be subject to the following requirements: 
(1)	One attached sign pertaining to the occupancy of the premises or commodities sold on the premises shall be permitted for each thoroughfare when more than one abuts the property. 
(2)	One detached sign pertaining to the occupancy of the premises or commodities sold on the premises shall be permitted for each thoroughfare when more than one abuts the property. 
(3)	In instances where the abutting thoroughfare is a designated state or federal highway, detached signs shall not exceed 250 square feet in area on any one such street or thoroughfare. 
(4)	In instances where the abutting thoroughfare is not a designated state or federal highway, detached signs shall not exceed 200 square feet in area on any one such street or thoroughfare. 
(5)	Signs with three or more surfaces or signs with circular or spherical surfaces shall be allowed only in L-1 and G-1 districts. The total surface area of such signs shall not exceed 300 square feet in area. 
(Ord. No. 1999-002, § 3(II), 2-25-1999)
Cross reference— Zoning, app. A.  
Sec. 70-164. - Shopping center and shopping mall signs. 
Signs for shopping centers and shopping malls shall be limited to: 
(1)	One attached sign per occupant of a shopping center or mall shall be permitted for each thoroughfare when more than one thoroughfare abuts the property. 
(2)	Only one detached sign, identifying the premises and/or its occupants, shall be permitted for each shopping center and/or mall. This detached sign may be a single sign or may be a composite of several signs erected on and supported by the same structure. 
(3)	Single detached signs for shopping centers and/or malls shall not exceed 250 square feet in area. 
(4)	The aggregate gross area of composite detached signs for shopping centers and/or malls shall not exceed 300 square feet, with no single sign exceeding 200 square feet in area. 
(5)	Detached signs for shopping centers and/or malls shall not be located closer than 25 feet to any street or thoroughfare. 
(6)	In shopping centers or malls containing ten acres or more, detached signs may be erected up to a maximum height of 75 feet; provided that such detached signs erected at a height greater than 50 feet must be set back from all property lines a minimum distance equal to the height of the sign. 
(Ord. No. 1999-002, § 3(III), 2-25-1999)
Cross reference— Businesses, ch. 18  
Chapter 74 - STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND OTHER PUBLIC PLACES 
FOOTNOTE(S):
