Cross reference— Any ordinance or resolution dedicating, naming, establishing, locating, relocating, opening, paving, widening, repairing, vacating, etc., any street or public way saved from repeal, § 1-10(a)(5); any ordinance levying or imposing taxes saved from repeal, § 1-10(a)(7); any ordinance prescribing through streets, parking and traffic regulations, speed limits, one-way traffic, limitations on load of vehicles or loading zones saved from repeal, § 1-10(a)(8); any ordinance establishing and prescribing the street grades of any street saved from repeal, § 1-10(a)(10); any ordinance providing for local improvements and assessing taxes for such improvements saved from repeal, § 1-10(a)(11); any ordinance authorizing street maintenance agreements saved from repeal, § 1-10(a)(17); aviation, ch. 10; buildings and building regulations, ch. 14; peddlers and solicitors, § 18-313; cemeteries, ch. 22; environment, ch. 34; distributing handbills on private property, § 34-36; flood prevention and protection, ch. 42; parks and recreation, ch. 62; signs, ch. 70; subdivisions, ch. 78; required improvements for street paving in subdivisions, § 78-111 et seq.; traffic and vehicles, ch. 86; specific street regulations, § 86-71 et seq.; utilities, ch. 90; vehicles for hire, ch. 94; zoning, app. A. 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 74-1. - Consumption of alcohol prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to consume any alcoholic beverage in any public place, or for any person to possess any alcoholic beverage in any public place for the purpose of consuming such alcoholic beverage in such public place, within the city limits. 
(Ord. No. 1984-0005, § I(3.1), 4-12-1984)
Cross reference— Alcoholic beverages, § 18-31 et seq.  
Secs. 74-2—74-30. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - STREETS  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Secs. 74-31—74-50. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - OBSTRUCTIONS  
Subdivision I. - In General 
 
Secs. 74-51—74-60. - Reserved.  
Subdivision II. - Clear Sight Visibility Triangle 
 
Sec. 74-61. - Areas regulated. 
(a)	The areas in the city which are subject to this subdivision are as follows:
(1)	Those street intersections controlled by a stop sign and railroad street intersections controlled by railroad traffic control devices. 
(2)	A triangular area established beginning with the point in the center of the street or railroad being intersected, that area being in the center of the intersection; then along a straight line from the center point along the intersected street or railroad for the distance set out in subsection (b) of this section; then along a straight line back to the stop sign, traffic control device, or railroad control device; then to the point of beginning at the center point, forming a triangle. 
(b)	The distances in feet mentioned in subsection (a) along the intersected street or railroad are as follows: 
	30mph	35mph	40mph	45mph	50mph	55mph
2-lane	300	350	400	450	500	550
4-lane	350	400	450	500	600	650
 
(Ord. No. 1979-0002, §§ I, II, 1-15-1979) 
Sec. 74-62. - Height limitations; exceptions. 
(a)	No property owner shall allow any object, vegetation, fence, structure, or any element, except grass or other landscaping or vegetation which can never grow to a height exceeding 2½ feet above the top of the curb elevation or three feet above the edge of the roadway where no curb exists, within the sight distance triangle as described in section 74-61 at any public and private street or railway intersections other than a street intersection controlled by a signal light within the city. 
(b)	The following shall be exempted from the restriction of subsection (a) of this section:
(1)	Single trunk trees when trimmed completely to a height of seven feet.
(2)	Signs when supported by a single post not exceeding one foot in diameter and such sign is at least ten feet above the top of the curb elevation, sidewalk elevation, or 10½ feet above the edge of the pavement where no curb or sidewalk exists. 
(3)	Utility poles installed under provisions of existing franchises within the city.
(Ord. No. 1979-0002, § III, 1-15-1979) 
Sec. 74-63. - Exceptions. 
The provisions of this subdivision shall not apply to any business building, family dwelling or apartment house existing in the city on January 15, 1979, and not in violation of any law of the state or ordinance of the city. 
(Ord. No. 1979-0002, § IV, 1-15-1979) 
Sec. 74-64. - Effect on city administration. 
The provisions of this subdivision shall have no bearing or effect upon the right of the city to administer and control the remaining portions of its public street rights-of-way not involved in the triangular corner areas provided for in this subdivision. 
(Ord. No. 1979-0002, § V, 1-15-1979) 
Secs. 74-65—74-100. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - EXCAVATIONS  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Sec. 74-101. - Placement of obstructions in gutter. 
No person shall place or have placed in the gutter of any street in the city any type of fixed object or matter, including driveway ramps. Placement of such obstruction in the gutter of any street in the city by any person will subject that person to the provisions of section 1-14, and that person will also be responsible for removal of the obstruction at his expense. 
(Ord. No. 1981-0015, § 9.67, 7-9-1981) 
Secs. 74-102—74-120. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - PERMIT 
 
Sec. 74-121. - Required. 
No person shall make any excavation of any kind under or across any alley, street, avenue, curb and gutter or sidewalk, without a special permit from the city after paying a fee on file in the city secretary's office; and while such excavation is open, he shall, at his own expense, place proper guide lamps and signal lights in and around the excavation, sufficient to warn the public of such excavation so that all persons using reasonable care shall be protected from accident, and will hold the city harmless against all claims growing out of the work. All cuts of curbs and sidewalks are subject to city review, with the city having the authority to location of all curb and sidewalk cuts. 
(Ord. No. 1981-0015, § 9.65, 7-9-1981) 
Sec. 74-122. - Restoring area to former condition. 
When any part of any street, avenue, curb and gutter, sidewalk or alley or other public place in the city shall be torn, dug up or taken up, for any purpose, the person doing such work shall, immediately upon the completion of such purpose and as fast as practicable during the accomplishment, return the earth and ram and paddle the earth to firm and solid bearing, and in such manner as will entirely present the settling of such earth, and shall also re-lay the paving, macadamizing or gravel in a skillful and permanent manner, and in every case to the entire satisfaction of the city's agent; and if such work is not done to the satisfaction of the city, the city may have it done at the expense of the permittee. 
(Ord. No. 1981-0015, § 9.66, 7-9-1981) 
Chapter 78 - SUBDIVISIONS 
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (1) --- 
Charter reference— Platting of property, § 11.01 
Cross reference— Any ordinance dedicating or accepting any plat or subdivision saved from repeal, § 1-10(a)(12); buildings and building regulations, ch. 14; environment, ch. 34; flood prevention and protection, ch. 42; streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 74; utilities, ch. 90; zoning, app. A; mobile home subdivision district, app. A, § 9-1 et seq..
State Law reference— Subdivisions, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 212.001 et seq. 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 78-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Plat means a map or chart of the subdivision. It includes plan, plat or replat, and includes both singular and plural. 
Resubdivision means the division of an existing subdivision, together with any change of lot size in the subdivision, or with the relocation of any street lines. 
Subdivision means the division of a tract or parcel of land into two or more parts or lots for the purpose, whether immediate or future, of sale or building development or transfer of ownership, and shall include resubdivision. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0006, § 1-2, 5-24-1994)
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2  
Sec. 78-2. - Scope. 
This chapter shall govern every person owning any tract of land within the city limits or within the extraterritorial jurisdiction of the city, who may hereafter divide the tract into two or more parts for the purpose of laying out any subdivision of any tract of land or any addition to the city, or for laying out suburban lots or building lots, or any lots, and streets, alleys or parks or other portions intended for public use, or the use of purchasers or owners of lots fronting on or adjacent to the tract. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0006, § 1-1, 5-24-1994) 
Sec. 78-3. - Policy. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any owner or agent of any owner of land to lay out, subdivide, plat or replat any land into lots, blocks and streets within the city or within the city's extraterritorial jurisdiction without the prior approval of the city planning commission. It shall also be unlawful for any such owner or agent to offer for sale or sell property which has not been laid out, subdivided, platted or replatted with the approval of the city planning commission. 
(b)	The city defines its policy to be that the city will withhold all city improvements of whatsoever nature, including the maintenance of streets and the furnishing of sewer facilities and water service from all additions and subdivisions, the platting of which has not been approved by the city planning commission. 
(c)	No street number and no building permit shall be issued for the erection of any building in the city on any place of property other than an original or resubdivided lot in a duly approved and recorded subdivision without the written approval of the planning commission. 
(d)	The attention of each subdivider is directed to V.T.C.A., Property Code § 12.002, which states in part: 
"The county clerk or a deputy of the clerk with whom a plat or replat of a subdivision of real property is filed for recording shall determine whether the plat or replat is required by law to be approved by a county or municipal authority or both. The clerk or deputy may not record a plat or replat requiring approval unless it is approved as provided by law by the appropriate authority…. If a plat or replat does not indicate whether land covered by the plat or replat is in the extraterritorial jurisdiction of the municipality, the county clerk may require the person filing the plat or replat for recording to file with the clerk an affidavit stating that information." 
(Ord. No. 1994-0006, § 1-3, 5-24-1994) 
Sec. 78-4. - General requirements. 
(a)	Streets in general must conform to the following:
(1)	Minimum right-of-way width of 60 feet; however, greater width may be required.
(2)	Shall connect with existing streets in adjoining subdivisions.
(3)	Be named to provide continuity with existing streets.
(4)	Avoid dead ends, except for future planning courts.
(5)	Platted with appropriate regard for all topographical features lending themselves to attractive treatment and layout of utilities. 
(b)	Alleys shall have minimum width of 15 feet.
(c)	Residential lots shall meet the requirements for the area's intended zoning designation of either R-1 or R-2 as defined by the city's zoning ordinance, appendix A to this Code. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0006, § 1-4, 5-24-1994) 
Sec. 78-5. - Survey requirements. 
(a)	Monuments consisting of three-eighths-inch re-rod, 18 inches in length shall be placed at all corners of the block lines, the point of intersection of curves and tangents of the subdivision. 
(b)	One benchmark for each five acres of property or fraction thereof shall be permanently installed in an approved manner, with their location and the elevation shown on the plat. 
(c)	Lot markers shall be metal or concrete placed at each corner of all lots, flush with the average ground elevation, or they may be countersunk, if necessary to avoid being disturbed. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0006, § 1-5, 5-24-1994) 
Sec. 78-6. - Authority. 
(a)	Where extraordinary hardship may result from strict compliance with this chapter, the planning commission or the city council may vary this chapter so that substantial justice may be done and the public interest secured; however, such variation shall not have the effect of nullifying the intent and purpose of this chapter. 
(b)	The city council may refuse to approve a plat unless it is evident that proper water and sewer facilities can be supplied within a reasonable length of time. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0006, § 1-9, 5-24-1994) 
Sec. 78-7. - As-built plans. 
The subdivider must provide to the city as-built plans for all paving, drainage, water lines and sewer lines within 30 days after completion of the project. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0006, § 1-10, 5-24-1994) 
Sec. 78-8. - Fees and charges. 
(a)	Fees and charges shall be paid into the general fund of the city when any map or plat is tendered to the city planning commission; and each of the fees and charges provided in this section shall be paid in advance; and no action of the city planning commission shall be valid until the fee shall have been paid. The city manager or his deputies or assistants shall calculate the fees and charges in accordance with the schedule on file in the city secretary's office. 
(b)	For approval of multiple dwelling areas, business, or industrial areas not subdivided into lots, both the preliminary and final plat shall carry a fee on file in the city secretary's office per acre. 
(c)	The fees shall be charged on all plats, regardless of the action by the city planning commission. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0006, § 1-11, 5-24-1994) 
Secs. 78-9—78-40. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - PLATS  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Secs. 78-41—78-60. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - PRELIMINARY PLATS 
 
Sec. 78-61. - Submission. 
Three copies of a preliminary plat shall be submitted to the city manager for presentation to the city planning commission five days prior to the meeting at which approval is asked. The plat shall be drawn to a scale of 200 feet to one inch or larger, and shall show or be accompanied by the following information: 
(1)	Name of subdivision.
(2)	Names of the owner and engineer or surveyor responsible for the survey and design.
(3)	Boundary lines, existing building lines, and width and location of platted streets and alleys within and adjacent to the property. 
(4)	Width and depth and/or area of proposed lots.
(5)	Physical features of the property, including location of watercourses, culverts, bridges, proposed drainage ditches and present structures, streets and alleys, highways, etc., including widths and names. 
(6)	A designation of the proposed uses of land within the subdivision.
(7)	Adequate off-street parking must be provided for lots set aside or planned for business, public or institution use. 
(8)	A map on a small scale must be presented to show the nearest subdivision, and how the streets, alleys or highways in the subdivision submitted may connect with those nearby. 
(9)	Profiles of streets and ditches may be called for.
(10)	In subdividing property, due consideration shall be given to suitable sites for schools, and to the dedication of parks and playgrounds. Such provision should be indicated on the preliminary plan in order that it may be determined when and in what manner such areas will be dedicated to the public use. Such property shall not be less desirable nature than other property in the subdivision. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0006, § 1-8(A), 5-24-1994) 
Sec. 78-62. - Action on preliminary plats by planning commission. 
(a)	Following a review of the preliminary plat and negotiations with the subdivider on changes deemed advisable and the kind and extent of improvements to be made by him, the planning commission shall, within 30 days, act on the changes as submitted or modified, and if approved shall express its approval as conditional approval and state the conditions of such approval, if any, or if disapproved, shall express its disapproval and the reasons for disapproval. 
(b)	The action of the planning commission shall be noted on three copies of the preliminary plat, referenced and attached to any conditions determined. One copy shall be returned to the subdivider, one copy presented to the city council and the third retained by the planning commission. 
(c)	Approval of the preliminary plat does not constitute acceptance of the subdivision but is merely authority to proceed with the preparation of the final or record plat. No work shall be done of the subdivision before the final plat is accepted and recorded. Approval of a preliminary plat expires at the end of 90 days unless final or record plat has been submitted to the city council. Any changes by the planning commission, the city engineer or other may require submission of another preliminary plat. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0006, § 1-8(B), 5-24-1994) 
Secs. 78-63—78-80. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 3. - FINAL PLAT 
 
Sec. 78-81. - Submittal. 
Two white print copies of the final or record plat with reproducible tracing of the final plat shall be submitted to the city council after the preliminary plat has been approved by the planning commission and all changes and alterations made. No final plat will be considered unless a preliminary plat has first been submitted and approved. Such plats shall be filed with the city manager at least five days prior to the meeting at which approval is requested. The final plat shall show or be accompanied by the following data: 
(1)	Plats shall be drawn upon sheets of 24 by 36 inches and to the scale of 100 feet to the inch. 
(2)	A title, including name of subdivision owners, and licensed land surveyor or registered engineer or registered public surveyor responsible for the plat, and the scale and location of the subdivision with reference to original land grants or surveys, the date and north point. 
(3)	The certificate of the registered engineer or licensed surveyor who surveyed, mapped and monumented the land should be placed on the face of the plat. 
(4)	A certificate of ownership and dedication of all streets, alleys, parks and playgrounds to public use forever, signed and acknowledged before a notary public by the owner and lienholder of the land. A complete and accurate description of the land subdivided and the street dedicated. 
(5)	An accurate on-the-ground boundary survey of the property with bearings and distances and showing the lines of all adjacent land, streets and alleys with their names and width. Streets, alleys and lot lines in adjacent subdivision shall be shown dotted. All necessary data to reproduce the plat on the ground must be shown on the plat. 
(6)	Approval of the preliminary plat signed by the city planning commission placed on the face of the plat. 
(7)	Two sets of plans and specifications for water, sewer, paving and drainage prepared by a registered civil engineer, which must be approved by the city council prior to the beginning of any construction in the subdivision. 
(8)	A letter from the appropriate drainage commission addressed to the city planning commission stating that plans for drainage of the subdivision are approved by the drainage commission. 
(9)	Coordination with servicing utility companies regarding the furnishing of utilities.
(10)	Two copies of deed restrictions.
(Ord. No. 1994-0006, § 1-8(C), 5-24-1994) 
Sec. 78-82. - Action on final plat by city council. 
(a)	Following a review of the final plat and when to the satisfaction of the city council all conditions and requirements have been met, the city council shall approve the final plat. 
(b)	Should the final plat as submitted fail to meet the conditions and requirements of the city council or fail to meet the previous recommendations of the planning commission, the city council shall disapprove the plat and note its disapproval on the plat, and attach to the plat a statement of reasons for disapproval. 
(c)	Approval or disapproval of the final plat shall be voted by the city council within 30 days after the submission of the final plat. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0006, § 1-8(D), 5-24-1994) 
Secs. 78-83—78-110. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - REQUIRED IMPROVEMENTS 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference— Streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 74  
Sec. 78-111. - Street paving. 
The subdivider shall improve all streets in the subdivision. Improvements shall be installed to a permanent line and grade and to the satisfaction of the city engineer. All street construction work shall be performed by a bonded contractor who has filed a faithful performance bond with the city. Approval of the plat shall not impose any duty upon the city concerning the maintenance of such improvements until the city shall have made actual acceptance of the improvements. The minimum improvements which the subdivider shall make, or agree to make, prior to acceptance and approval of the final plat by the city council shall be: 
(1)	Grading, drainage and drainage structures necessary to properly drain the area.
(2)	Pavements of a width suitable for the traffic on the street.
(3)	Curb and gutter of 2,500 pounds per square inch concrete.
(Ord. No. 1994-0006, § 1-6(A), 5-24-1994) 
Sec. 78-112. - Utilities. 
The minimum improvements which the subdivider shall make, or agree to make, prior to acceptance and approval of the final plat by the city council shall be: 
(1)	Water systems with mains of sufficient size and having a sufficient number of outlets to furnish adequate domestic water supply, furnish fire protection to all lots and to meet the requirements of the city. 
(2)	Sanitary sewer facilities to service the subdivision and meet the requirements of the city. 
(3)	All services for utilities shall be made available for each lot in such a manner as will obviate the necessity for disturbing the street paving, gutter, curb and drainage structures when connections are made. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0006, § 1-6(B), 5-24-1994)
Cross reference— Utilities, ch. 90  
Sec. 78-113. - Paving and utilities. 
The subdivider shall award the contract and make payments directly to the contractor after the plans and specifications have been approved by the city council for all grading, paving, drainage structures and utilities in the subdivision. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0006, § 1-7, 5-24-1994)
Cross reference— Utilities, ch. 90

ARTICLE III. - HOTEL OCCUPANCY TAX 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (3) --- 
Cross reference— Businesses, ch. 18 
State Law reference— Hotel occupancy tax, V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 351.001 et seq. 
Sec. 82-61. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Consideration means the cost of the room in a hotel only if the room is ordinarily used for sleeping, and not including the cost of any food served or personal services rendered to the occupant of such room not related to the cleaning and readying of such room for occupancy. 
Hotel means a building in which members of the public obtain sleeping accommodations for consideration. The term includes a hotel, motel, tourist home, tourist house, tourist court, lodginghouse, inn, roominghouse, or bed and breakfast. The term does not include a: 
(1)	Hospital, sanitarium or nursing home; or
(2)	Dormitory or other housing facility owned or leased and operated by an institution of higher education or a private or independent institution of higher education as those terms are defined by V.T.C.A., Education Code § 61.003, used by the institution for the purpose of providing sleeping accommodations for persons engaged in an educational program or activity at the institution. 
Occupancy means the use or possession, or the right to the use or possession, of any room in a hotel if the room is one which is ordinarily used for sleeping and if the occupant is other than a permanent resident. 
Occupant means anyone who, for a consideration, uses or possesses any room in a hotel under any lease, concession, permit, rite of access, license, contract or agreement, other than a permanent resident. 
Permanent resident means any occupant who has or shall have the right to occupancy of any room in a hotel for at least 30 consecutive days during the calendar year or preceding year and there is no interruption in the payment for that period. 
Tax assessor-collector means the tax assessor and collector of the city. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0017, § 13.3, 12-13-1994)
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, V.T.C.A., Tax Code §§ 156.001, 156.051.  
Sec. 82-62. - Levied; amount. 
There is levied a tax of seven percent of the price paid for a room in a hotel on every person who, under a lease, concession, permit, right of access, license, contract or agreement, pays for the use or possession or for the right to the use or possession of a room that is in a hotel, cost $25.00 or more each day, and is ordinarily used for sleeping. The price of a room in a hotel does not include the cost of food served by the hotel and the cost of personal services performed by the hotel for the person except those services related to the cleaning and readying of the room for possession. No tax shall be imposed on a permanent resident as defined in section 82-61. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0017, § 13.4, 12-13-1994; Ord. of 6-25-1998) 
Sec. 82-63. - Exemptions. 
(a)	A United States governmental entity described in V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 156.103(a) is exempt from the payment of tax authorized by this article. 
(b)	A state governmental entity described in V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 156.103(b) shall pay the tax imposed by this article but is entitled to a refund of the tax paid. 
(c)	A person who is described by V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 156.103(d) is exempt from the payment of the tax authorized by this article. 
(d)	A person who is described by V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 156.103(c) shall pay the tax imposed by this article but the state governmental entity with whom the person is associated is entitled to a refund of the tax paid. 
(e)	To receive a refund of tax paid under this article, the governmental entity entitled to the refund must file a refund claim on a form provided by the city and containing the information required by the city. The state comptroller by rule shall prescribe the form that must be used and the information that must be provided. 
(f)	A governmental entity may file a refund claim with the city under this article only for each calendar quarter for all reimbursements accrued during that quarter. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0017, § 13.4, 12-13-1994) 
Sec. 82-64. - Collection of tax. 
Every person owning, operating, managing or controlling any hotel shall collect the tax levied by this article for the city. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0017, § 13.5, 12-13-1994) 
Sec. 82-65. - Quarterly reports to tax assessor-collector. 
On the last day of the month, every person required to collect the tax imposed by this article shall file a report with the assessor-collector of taxes showing the price paid for all room occupancies in the preceding quarter, the amount of tax collected on such occupancies, and any other information the assessor-collector may reasonably require. Such person shall pay the tax due on such occupancies at the time of filing such report. The report shall be in a form prescribed by the assessor-collector. The assessor-collector is authorized and directed to do all such things necessary or convenient to carry out the terms of this article. The assessor-collector shall have the authority to request and receive within a reasonable time documentation for information contained in the report by the hotel. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0017, § 13.6, 12-13-1994) 
Sec. 82-66. - Rules and regulations of tax assessor-collector; access to books and records. 
The assessor-collector shall have the power to make such rules and regulations as are reasonable and necessary to effectively collect the tax levied by this article and shall upon reasonable notice have access to books and records necessary to enable him to determine the correctness of any report filed as required by this article and the amount of taxes due under the provisions of this article. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0017, § 13.7, 12-13-1994) 
Sec. 82-67. - Penalties. 
(a)	If any person shall fail to file a report as required in this article or shall file a false report or shall fail to pay to the tax assessor-collector the tax as imposed in this article when the report of payment is due, he shall forfeit five percent of the amount due as penalty; and after the first 30 days, he shall forfeit an additional five percent of such tax. However, such penalty shall never be less than $1.00. Delinquent taxes shall draw interest at the rate of ten percent per annum beginning 60 days from the due date. 
(b)	Any person violating any of the provisions of this article, including hotel operators who fail to collect the tax, fail to file a return, file a false return, or who are delinquent in their tax payment, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall upon conviction be fined as provided in section 1-14 
(Ord. No. 1994-0017, § 13.8, 12-13-1994) 
Sec. 82-68. - Additional penalties. 
The city is authorized to take the following actions against any person required to collect the tax imposed by this article and pay the collection over to the city and who has failed to file a report, or filed a false report, or failed to pay the tax when due: 
(1)	Bring suit against the hotel for noncompliance; and/or
(2)	Bring suit against the hotel seeking any other remedies provided under state law.
(Ord. No. 1994-0017, § 13.9, 12-13-1994) 
Sec. 82-69. - Additional authorization to bring suit. 
The city attorney is authorized to bring suit against any person required to collect the tax imposed by this article and required to pay the collection over to the city and who has failed to file a report, or filed a false report, or failed to pay the tax when due. Such suit may seek to collect such tax not paid or to enjoin such person from operating a hotel in the city until the tax is paid or the report is filed or both, as applicable and as provided in the injunction. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0017, § 13.10, 12-13-1994) 
Sec. 82-70. - Use of revenue derived from levy of hotel occupancy tax. 
(a)	The revenue derived from any hotel occupancy tax imposed and levied by this article may be used only to promote tourism and the convention and hotel industry, and that use is limited to the following: 
(1)	The acquisition of sites for and the construction, improvement, enlarging, equipping, repairing, operation and maintenance of convention center facilities (as such is defined in V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 351.001); 
(2)	The furnishing of facilities, personnel and materials for the registration of convention delegates or registrants; 
(3)	Advertising and conducting solicitations and promotional programs to attract tourists and convention delegates or registrants to the city or its vicinity; 
(4)	The encouragement, promotion, improvement and application of the arts, including instrumental and vocal music, dance, drama, folk art, creative writing, architecture, design and allied fields, painting, sculpture, photography, graphic and craft arts, motion pictures, radio, television, tape and sound recording, and other arts related to the presentation, performance, execution and exhibition of these major art forms; and 
(5)	Historical restoration and preservation projects or activities or advertising and conducting solicitations and promotional programs to encourage tourists and convention delegates to visit preserved historic sites or museums which are: 
a.	At or in the immediate vicinity of convention center facilities; or
b.	Located elsewhere in the city or its vicinity that would be frequented by tourists, convention delegates or other visitors to the city. 
(b)	Revenue derived from the hotel occupancy tax shall be expended only in a manner which directly enhances and promotes tourism and the convention and hotel industry as delineated in subsection (a) of this section. Such revenue shall not be used for the general revenue purposes or general governmental operations of the city which are not directly related to promoting the hotel and convention industry or tourism in the city. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0017, § 13.11, 12-13-1994) 
Sec. 82-71. - Administrative requirements; accountability; keeping of records. 
(a)	The city council may, by contract, delegate to a person, including another governmental entity or a private organization, the management or supervision of programs and activities funded with revenue from the hotel occupancy tax. The city council shall approve in writing in advance the annual budget of the entity to which it delegates those functions and shall require the entity to make periodic reports to the city council at least annually, listing the expenditures made by the entity of revenue from the tax provided by the city. 
(b)	The entity must maintain the revenue provided by the city from the tax in a separate account established for that purpose and may not commingle that revenue with any other money or maintain it in any other account. 
(c)	The city may not delegate to any person or entity the management or supervision of its convention and visitors programs and activities funded with revenue from the hotel occupancy tax other than by contract as provided in this article. 
(d)	The approval by the city council of the annual budget of the entity to which these functions are delegated creates a fiduciary duty in the person or entity with respect to the revenue provided by the city to the person or entity under the contract. 
(e)	A person or entity with whom the city contracts to conduct authorized activities shall maintain complete and accurate financial records of each expenditure of hotel occupancy tax revenue made by the person or entity and, on request of the city council or other person, shall make the records available for inspection and review. 
(f)	Hotel occupancy tax revenue may be spent for day-to-day operations, supplies, salaries, office rental, travel expenses and other administrative costs only if those administrative costs are incurred directly in the promotion and servicing of expenditures previously authorized. The portion of the total administrative costs for activities for which hotel occupancy tax revenue may be used may not exceed the administrative costs actually incurred in conducting the authorized activities. 
(g)	Hotel occupancy tax revenue may not be spent for travel for a person to attend an event or conduct an activity the primary purpose of which is not directly related to the promotion of the person's job in an efficient and professional manner. 
(Ord. No. 1994-0017, § 13.12, 12-13-1994) 
Secs. 82-72—82-100. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE IV. - OCCUPATION TAX

Sec. 82-101. - Levied. 
As provided in the Texas Constitution, art. VIII, § 1, the city council levies an occupation tax of half the amount of the state occupation tax authorized in state law. 
(Ord. No. 1960-0002) 
Chapter 86 - TRAFFIC AND VEHICLES 
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Operation of vehicles on runways restricted, § 10-102; litter from trucks, § 34-33; handbills on vehicles, § 34-35; abandoned motor vehicles, § 34-211 et seq.; junked vehicles, § 34-231 et seq.; law enforcement, ch. 50; miscellaneous offenses, ch. 54; streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 74; vehicles for hire, ch. 94 
State Law reference— Rules of the road, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 541.001 et seq. 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 86-1. - Roller skates, coasters, skateboards, bicycles and similar vehicles prohibited in central business district. 
No person shall ride in, ride upon, or in any manner operate any roller skates, coaster, skateboard, toy vehicle, bicycles, or like vehicle or device upon any sidewalk, roadway and/or street within the central business district of the city. The provisions of this section shall not apply to wheelchairs or other devices designed to aid handicapped or impaired persons. For the purposes of this section, the central business district shall be defined as that portion of the city bounded by Highway 271 on the east, Cass Street on the north, Montgomery Street on the west and Butler Street on the south. 
(Ord. No. 1995-0016, § 1, 7-18-1995)
Cross reference— Businesses, ch. 18; zoning, app. A. 
State Law reference— Authority to regulate time, place and manner of roller skating on a street, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 542.202(5).  
Sec. 86-2. - Engine retarding braking devices. 
The use of engine retarding braking devices is prohibited within the city limits. Violation of this section shall constitute a misdemeanor and upon conviction a fine shall be levied not to exceed the maximum allowed by law. 
(Ord. No. 2003-012, 11-18-2003)
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2003-012, adopted November 18, 2003, did not specify manner of inclusion, hence, inclusion as § 86-2 is at the discretion of the editor.  
Secs. 86-3—86-30. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Traffic control devices, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 544.001 et seq. 
Sec. 86-31. - Conformity with state rules. 
All traffic control devices, including signs, signals and markings on pavement and/or curb installed or used for the purpose of directing and controlling traffic within the city shall conform with the Texas Manual on Uniform Traffic Control Devices for Streets and Highways, volumes I and II. All signs, signals and markings erected or used by the city shall be uniform and be located so far as practicable according to the directions shown in the manual throughout the city. 
(Ord. No. 1978-0009, § 1, 11-14-1978)
State Law reference— Sign manual, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 544.001.  
Sec. 86-32. - Obedience required; exceptions. 
The driver of any vehicle, motor vehicle or animal shall obey the instructions of any applicable official traffic control device, sign, signal or marking placed in accordance with this article, unless otherwise directed by a police officer, subject to the exceptions granted the driver of an authorized emergency vehicle permitted by this article. 
(Ord. No. 1978-0009, § 2, 11-14-1978) 
Sec. 86-33. - Applicability to authorized emergency vehicles. 
(a)	The driver of an authorized emergency vehicle, as that term is defined by state law, when responding to an emergency call or when in the pursuit of an actual or suspected violator of the law, or when responding to but not upon returning from a fire alarm, may exercise the privileges set forth in this section, but subject to the conditions stated in this section. 
(b)	The driver of an authorized emergency vehicle may:
(1)	Park or stand, irrespective of the provisions of this section or any ordinance.
(2)	Proceed past a red or stop signal or stop sign, but only after slowing down as may be necessary for safe operation. 
(3)	Exceed the prima facie speed limits so long as he does not endanger life or property.
(4)	Disregard regulations governing direction of movement or turning in specified directions.
(c)	The exemptions granted in this section to an authorized emergency vehicle shall apply only when such vehicle is making use of audible and visual signals meeting the requirements of V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 547.702, except that an authorized emergency vehicle operated as a police vehicle need not be equipped with or display a red light visible from the front of the vehicle. 
(d)	The provisions of subsections (a)—(c) of this section shall not relieve the driver of an authorized emergency vehicle from the duty to drive with due regard for the safety of all persons, nor shall such provisions protect the driver from the consequences of his reckless disregard for the safety of others. 
(e)	Provisions of this article applicable to drivers upon the highways shall apply to the drivers of all vehicles owned or operated by the United States; the state; or any county, city, town, district or any other political subdivision of the state, subject to such specific exceptions as are set forth in this article with reference to authorized emergency vehicles. 
(Ord. No. 1978-0009, § 3, 11-14-1978)
State Law reference— Emergency vehicles, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code §§ 545.156, 545.365, 546.001 et seq.  
Sec. 86-34. - Unauthorized signs prohibited. 
(a)	No person shall place, maintain or display upon or in view of any highway, street or alley any unauthorized sign, signal, marking or device which purports to be or is an imitation of or resembles an official traffic control device or railroad sign or signal, or which attempts to direct the movement of traffic, or which hides from view or interferes with the effectiveness of any official control device or any railroad sign or signal. 
(b)	No person shall place or maintain nor shall any public authority permit upon any highway, street or alley any traffic sign or signal bearing any commercial advertising. 
(c)	This section shall not be deemed to prohibit the erection upon private property adjacent to highways, streets or alleys of signs giving useful directional information and of a type that cannot be mistaken for official signs. 
(d)	Every such prohibited sign, signal or marking is declared to be a public nuisance, and the chief of police is empowered to remove it or cause it to be moved without notice. 
(Ord. No. 1978-0009, § 4, 11-14-1978)
State Law reference— Similar provisions, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 544.006.  
Sec. 86-35. - Damaging signs prohibited. 
No person shall without lawful authority attempt to or in fact alter, deface, injure, knock down or remove any official traffic control device, sign or signal or any railroad sign or signal or any inscription, shield, or insignia on or any part of such device, sign or signal. 
(Ord. No. 1978-0009, § 5, 11-14-1978)
State Law reference— Similar provisions, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 544.005.  
Sec. 86-36. - Prima facie evidence of validity. 
It shall be unlawful for any person other than the city manager or his designee, acting pursuant to an ordinance of the city, to install or cause to be installed any signal, sign or device purporting to direct the use of the streets or the activities on those streets of pedestrians, vehicles, motor vehicles, or animals, proof, in any prosecution for a violation of this article or any traffic ordinance of the city that any traffic control device, sign, signal or marking was actually in place on any street shall constitute prima facie evidence that it was installed by the city manager or his designee pursuant to the authority of this article and of the ordinance directing the installation of such device, signal or marking. 
(Ord. No. 1978-0009, § 7, 11-14-1978) 
Sec. 86-37. - Erection. 
(a)	The city council shall by ordinance direct that the city manager or his designee shall have the duty of erecting or installing upon, over, along or beside any highway, street or alley signs, signals and markings, or cause them to be erected, installed or placed in accordance with this article and consistent with the state manual adopted in section 86-31. Such traffic control devices shall be installed immediately or as soon as such specific device, sign or signal can be procured. 
(b)	Whenever the city manager or his designee has erected and installed any official traffic control device, signal or sign at any location in the city or has caused the same to be done under his direction, in obedience to this article and the state manual shall thereafter file a report with the city secretary in writing and signed officially by the city manager or his designee, stating the type of traffic control device, sign or signal, and when and where it was erected and installed. The city secretary shall file and maintain such report of the city manager or his designee among the official papers of the office of the city secretary. 
(Ord. No. 1978-0009, § 6, 11-14-1978)
State Law reference— Authority to place and maintain signs, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 544.002.  
Secs. 86-38—86-70. - Reserved.

DIVISION 2. - ONE-WAY STREETS 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (4) --- 
State Law reference— Authority to designate one-way streets, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 542.202(10). 
Sec. 86-91. - Designated. 
The following areas are designated one-way streets: 
(1)	Allen Street from Buffalo Street north to Scott Street during the hours of 7:30 a.m. to 8:30 a.m. and 2:00 p.m. to 4:00 p.m., on all days during which school is in session at the Gilmer Elementary School, with all traffic on Allen Street being directed in a northerly direction from Buffalo Street to Scott Street during these hours. 
(2)	Bledsoe Street from Scott Street south to Cass Street during the hours of 7:30 a.m. to 8:30 a.m. and 2:00 p.m. to 4:00 p.m., on all days during which school is in session at the Gilmer Elementary School, with all traffic on Bledsoe Street being directed in a southerly direction from Scott Street to Cass Street during these hours. 
(3)	Silver Alley between Harrison Street and Tyler Street all the time.
(Ord. No. 1980-0013, § 14.3, 10-9-1980) 
Secs. 86-92—86-110. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 3. - SPEED LIMITS 
 
Sec. 86-111. - Speed limit on Old Coffeeville Road. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to drive any automobile, motor scooter or any type of motor vehicle in excess of 30 miles per hour on Old Coffeeville Road from Highway 271 and Old Coffeeville Road to the southwestern side of the intersection of Oasis Street and Old Coffeeville Road. 
(Ord. No. 1984-0004, 4-12-1984; Ord. No. 2001-003, 4-12-2001) 
Sec. 86-112. - Speed limit on South Montgomery Street. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to drive any automobile, motor scooter or any type of motor vehicle in excess of 30 miles per hour on South Montgomery Street from the city limits on the south to the northern side of the intersection of Warren Avenue and South Montgomery Street. 
(Ord. No. 1984-0004, 4-12-1984; Ord. No. 2001-003, 4-12-2001) 
Sec. 86-113. - Speed limit on Scott Street, Bledsoe Street, Buffalo Street, Bruce Street and Bradford Street. 
(a)	For traffic traveling in either direction on Bruce Street from its intersection with State Highway 300 to its intersection with State Highway 271, the speed limit shall be 20 miles per hour from 7:30 a.m. to 8:30 a.m. and 2:00 p.m. to 4:00 p.m., on all days during which school is in session at the Gilmer Junior High School. 
(b)	For traffic traveling in a westerly direction on Buffalo Street from its intersection with Bradford Street to the intersection of REA Road, the speed limit shall be 20 miles per hour from 7:30 a.m. to 8:30 a.m. and 2:00 p.m. to 4:00 p.m., on all days during which school is in session at the Gilmer High School. 
(c)	For traffic traveling in an easterly direction on Buffalo Street from its intersection with REA Road to its intersection with Bradford Street, the speed limit shall be 20 miles per hour from 7:30 a.m. to 8:30 a.m. and 2:00 p.m. to 4:00 p.m., on all days during which school is in session at the Gilmer High School. 
(d)	For traffic traveling in a northerly direction on Bradford Street from its intersection with Buffalo Street to its intersection with Scott Street, the speed limit shall be 20 miles per hour from 7:30 a.m. to 8:30 a.m. and 2:00 p.m. to 4:00 p.m., on all days during which school is in session at the Gilmer High School. 
(e)	For traffic traveling in a southerly direction on Bradford Street from its intersection with Scott Street to its intersection with Bradford Street, the speed limit shall be 20 miles per hour from 7:30 a.m. to 8:30 a.m. and 2:00 p.m. to 4:00 p.m., on all days during which school is in session at the Gilmer High School. 
(Ord. No. 1981-0001, 1-5-1981) 
Sec. 86-114. - Travel on U.S. 271. 
(a)	For traffic traveling in a southerly direction on U.S. 271:
(1)	Sixty miles per hour from the north city limits (MP 10.998-Cont. 248-04), south for a distance of 0.283 miles, to a point 945 feet north of Harvey St. (MP 11.281-Cont. 248-04) except for that portion from a point at the north city limits (MP 10.998 Cont. 248-04) south for a distance of 0.283 miles, to a point 945 feet north of Harvey St. (MP 11.281-cont. 248-04) the speed limit shall be 35 miles per hour when the school speed zone flashing beacons are in operation on school days. 
(2)	Fifty-five miles per hour from a point 945 feet north of Harvey St. (MP 11.281-Cont. 248-04) south for a distance of 0.257 miles, to a point 190 feet north of Yamboree Grounds Dr. (MP 11.538-Cont. 248-04). 
(3)	Forty-five miles per hour from a point 190 feet north of Yamboree Grounds Dr. (MP 11.538-Cont. 248-04) south for a distance of 0.582 miles, to a point 100 feet north of Coffeeville Rd. (MP 12.120-Cont. 248-04). 
(4)	Forty miles per hour from a point 100 feet north of Coffeeville Rd. (MP 12.120-Cont. 248-04) south for a distance of 1.230 miles, to a point 486 feet north of Warren Ave. (MP 12.449-Cont. 248-05). 
(5)	Forty-five miles per hour from a point 486 feet north of Warren Ave. (MP 12.449-Cont. 248-05) south for a distance of 0.776 miles, to a point 544 feet south of Dean St. (MP 13.225-Cont. 248-05) except for that portion from a point 850 feet south of Warren Ave. (MP 12.702-Cont. 248-05) south for a distance of 0.209 miles, to a point 264 feet north of SH 300 (MP 12.911-Cont. 248-05) the speed limit shall be 35 miles per hour when the school speed zone flashing beacons are in operation on school days. 
(6)	Fifty-five miles per hour from a point 544 feet south of Dean St. (MP 13.225-Cont. 248-05) south for a distance of 0.563 miles, to a point 3,464 feet south of Dean St. (MP 13.778-Cont. 248-05). 
(7)	Sixty miles per hour from a point 3,464 feet south of Dean St. (MP 13.788-Cont. 248-05) south for a distance of 0.376 miles, to a point 5,502 feet south of Dean St. (MP 14.164-Cont. 248-05) said point being the south city limits also point of termination. 
(b)	For traffic traveling in a northerly direction on U.S. 271.
(1)	Sixty miles per hour from the south city limits (MP 14.164-Cont. 248-05) north for a distance of 0.376 miles, to a point 3,464 feet south of Dean St. (MP 13.788-Cont. 248.05). 
(2)	Fifty-five miles per hour from a point 3.464 feet south of Dean St. (MP 13.778-Cont. 248-05) north for a distance of 0.563 miles, to a point 544 feet south of Dean St. (MP 13.225-cont. 248-05). 
(3)	Forty-five miles per hour from a point 544 feet south of Dean St. (MP 13.225-Cont. 248-05) north for a distance of 0.776 miles, to a point 486 feet north of Warren Ave. (MP 12.449-Cont. 248-05) except for that portion from a point 264 feet north of SH 300 (MP 12.911-cont. 248-05) north for a distance of 0.209 miles, to a point 850 feet south of Warren Ave. (MP 12.702-Cont. 248-05) the speed limit shall be 35 miles per hour when the school speed zone flashing beacons are in operation on school days. 
(4)	Forty miles per hour from a point 486 feet north of Warren Ave. (MP 12.449-Cont. 248-05) north for a distance of 1.230 miles, to a point 100 feet north of Coffeeville Rd. (MP 12-120-Cont. 248.04). 
(5)	Forty-five miles per hour from a point 100 feet north of Coffeeville Rd. (MP 12.120-Cont. 248-04) north for a distance of 0.582 miles, to a point 190 feet north of Yamboree Dr. (MP 11.538-Cont. 248-04). 
(6)	Fifty-five miles per hour from a point 190 feet north of Yamboree Dr. (MP 11.538-Cont. 248-04) north for a distance of 0.257 miles, to a point 945 feet north of Harvey St. (MP 11.281-Cont. 248-04). 
(7)	Sixty miles per hour from a point 945 feet north of Harvey St. (MP 11.281-Cont. 248-04) north for a distance of 0.283 miles, to a point 2,439 feet north of Harvey St. (MP 10.998-cont. 248-04) said point being the north city limits and also point of termination except for that portion from a point 945 feet north of Harvey St. (MP 11.281-Cont. 248-04) north for a distance of 0.283 miles, to a point 2,439 feet north of Harvey St. (MP 10.998-cont. 248-04) the speed limit shall be 35 miles per hour when the school speed zone flashing beacons are in operation on school days. 
(c)	The hereinabove speeds for vehicular traffic traveling upon the hereinabove designated section of U.S. 271 in the direction herein specified be and they are hereby found to be reasonable and safe prima fascia speed limits therefore. The fact that this regulation of the speed of motor vehicles is needed, creates and emergency which is for the immediate preservation of public safety and general welfare, requires that this ordinance take effect immediately from and after its passage and it is accordingly so ordained. 
(d)	The state department of transportation is authorized to erect signs indicating the speed limits herein designated. 
(Ord. No. 1999-011, §§ 1—3, 10-14-1999; Ord. No. 2007-001, §§ 1—3, 1-9-2007) 
Secs. 86-115—86-130. - Reserved.

ARTICLE IV. - STOPPING, STANDING, PARKING 
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (6) --- 
Cross reference— Off-street parking and loading requirements, app. A, § 16-11; parking, storage, keeping of commercial and recreational vehicles, app. A, § 16-12 
State Law reference— Authority to regulate stopping, standing or parking, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 542.202(2). 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Sec. 86-161. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Central business district means the geographical area encompassed by the following boundaries: Cass Street on the north, Harrison Street on the south, Trinity Street on the west, and up to but not including Highway No. 271 on the east. 
Operator means and includes any individual who shall operate a vehicle as its owner or as the agent, employee or permittee of the owner. 
Park and parking mean the standing of a vehicle, whether occupied or not. 
Street means any public street, avenue, road, boulevard, highway or other public place located in the city, and established for the use of vehicles. 
Vehicle means any device in, upon or by which any person or property is or may be transported or drawn upon a street or highway, except those operated upon rails or tracks. 
(Ord. No. 1983-0038, § 14.20, 12-22-1983)
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2  
Sec. 86-162. - Parking over the time limit in central business district. 
It shall be unlawful and an offense for any person to permit a vehicle to remain in a parking space within the central business district for a period in excess of the posted time limit, or if not posted, in excess of two hours. 
(Ord. No. 1983-0038, § 14.22, 12-22-1983) 
Sec. 86-163. - Parking within designated spaces in central business district. 
(a)	Any vehicle parked within the central business district shall be parked within the lines designating individual parking spaces. It shall be unlawful and an offense to park any vehicle in such a manner that the vehicle is not wholly contained within the lines designating individual parking spaces. 
(b)	The city manager or his designee shall place lines on the streets and/or curbs within the central business district clearly marking individual parking spaces. 
(Ord. No. 1983-0038, § 14.24, 12-22-1983) 
Sec. 86-164. - Exempted parking zones. 
(a)	The city council, or such officer or employee as they may designate, is authorized to establish theater and such other zones as are required by law, and to alter and/or exempt such zones from the provisions of this article. 
(b)	It shall be unlawful for any person to occupy or park a vehicle in the zones designated pursuant to the authority of subsection (a) of this section for any reason whatsoever. 
(Ord. No. 1983-0038, § 14.25, 12-22-1983) 
Sec. 86-165. - Declaring nuisance. 
(a)	No person shall allow, suffer or permit any vehicle registered in their name or subject to their control to be parked within the central business district or upon any street within the city limits in violation of any of the provisions regulating the parking of vehicles. 
(b)	If any vehicle is found within the central business district or upon any street within the city limits in violation of any of the provisions regulating vehicles and if the identity of the driver cannot be determined within a reasonable period of time, the vehicle may be declared a nuisance; and the registered owner or other person who has the vehicle subject to his control may be held responsible for such violation. 
(Ord. No. 1983-0038, § 14.26, 12-22-1983) 
Sec. 86-166. - Duty of police officers. 
It shall be the duty of each police officer and/or parking patrol officer, who shall observe a vehicle violating the time limits as specified in section 86-162, to note the vehicle's state license number, the time and date of such offense, make of the vehicle, and to issue in writing on such form as may be provided by the city a notice to be conspicuously placed on the vehicle, advising the operator to answer to the offense of violation of section 86-162 within 48 hours of the date of issuance of the notice at the location and time specified in the notice. 
(Ord. No. 1983-0038, § 14.23, 12-22-1983) 
Secs. 86-167—86-190. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - SPECIFIC PLACES 
 
Sec. 86-191. - Parking within central business district. 
(a)	No vehicle shall remain parked within the central business district for a period longer than is designated by sign or as is provided at any time between the hours of 8:00 a.m. and 5:00 p.m. of any day of the week except Sundays. 
(b)	It shall be unlawful and an offense for any vehicle transporting flammable and/or toxic substances to park within the central business district at any time. 
(c)	It shall be unlawful and an offense for any person to utilize a parking space within the central business district to park any vehicle when such person is utilizing the vehicle to sell, aid in the sale or store items that the person is selling or attempting to sell to the public. 
(Ord. No. 1983-0038, §§ 14.21, 14.38, 14.40, 12-22-1983) 
Sec. 86-192. - Parking on Cass Street. 
It shall be unlawful for any person at any time to park or leave any motor vehicle or any other object on the south side of Cass Street in the city between Trinity Street and the intersection of Wood Street, which is U.S. Highway No. 271. 
(Ord. No. 1983-0038, § 14.27, 12-22-1983) 
Sec. 86-193. - Parking on Scott Street. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to park or leave parked any motor vehicle or other vehicle on the north side of Scott Street between Bledsoe Street and Allen Street from 7:00 a.m. to 4:30 p.m., on all days during which school is in session at the Gilmer Elementary School. 
(Ord. No. 1983-0038, § 14.33, 12-22-1983) 
Sec. 86-194. - Parking on Bledsoe Street. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to park or leave parked any motor vehicle or other vehicle on the east side of Bledsoe Street between Scott Street and Cass Street from 7:00 a.m. to 4:30 p.m., on all days during which school is in session at the Gilmer Elementary School. 
(Ord. No. 1983-0038, § 14.34, 12-22-1983) 
Sec. 86-195. - Parking on Allen Street. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to park or leave parked any motor vehicle or other vehicle on the east and west side of Allen Street from the intersection of Cass Street and Scott Street from 7:00 a.m. to 4:30 p.m. on all days in which school is in session at the Gilmer Elementary School, except for loading or unloading students. 
(Ord. No. 1984-0002, 2-9-1984) 
Sec. 86-196. - Parking on Buffalo Street. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to park or leave parked any motor vehicle or other vehicle on the north side of Buffalo Street between the Gilmer High School Gymnasium and the creek, a total of 513 feet, at any time, and on the south side of Buffalo Street between Bradford Street on the east and the REA Road on the west from 6:00 a.m. to 4:00 p.m. on all days during which school is in session at the Gilmer High School. 
(Ord. No. 1990-005, § 14.41, 3-13-1990) 
Sec. 86-197. - Parking on Wood Street. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to park or leave parked any motor vehicle or other vehicles on either side of Wood Street in the city, which is U.S. Highway No. 271, between the south municipal boundary to the intersection of State Highway No. 155 on the north. The state highway department is charged with the installation of the appropriate signs on the street or on the curbs bearing the words "NO PARKING." 
(Ord. No. 1955-0008, § 1, 10-13-1955) 
Sec. 86-198. - Parking on Tyler Street and Montgomery Street. 
The following parking restrictions are placed in effect: 
(1)	No parking at any time on S.H. 154 (Tyler Street) from Montgomery Street to the St. Louis & Southwestern Railroad Grade Crossing and from Montgomery Street to a point approximately 225 feet west from the center of Montgomery Street. 
(2)	No parking at any time on Montgomery Street on either side for a distance of 20 feet from the crosswalk at intersection of Tyler Street and Montgomery Street and other parking on Montgomery Street to be restricted to parallel parking on one side only for one block north and south of S.H. 154 (Tyler Street); except that off street parking shall be permitted between the gutter line and sidewalk on the east side of Montgomery Street north of Highway 154 (Tyler Street). 
(3)	No parking at any time for a distance of 100 feet from the crosswalk on the west side of Montgomery Street north of Highway 154 and on the east side of Montgomery Street south of Highway 154 (Tyler Street). 
(Ord. No. 1956-0005, § 1, 11-14-1957) 
Sec. 86-199. - Parking on Chandler Street and Simpson Street. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to park or leave parked any motor vehicle or other vehicle at any time on the following named streets of the city: 
(1)	On Chandler Street from Marshall Street to Harrison Street.
(2)	On Simpson Street from Buffalo Street to Cass Street.
(Ord. No. 1958-0001, § 1, 3-13-1958) 
Sec. 86-200. - No parking zones. 
(a)	There is designated certain areas of the streets and/or alleys of the city as no parking zones. At no time may a vehicle be parked on either side of a street or alley designated as a no parking zone. 
(b)	The following areas are designated as no parking zones:
(1)	Dean Street, north side, from South Wood Street west to South Montgomery Street. 
(2)	Warren Street, south side, from South Wood Street west to St. Louis and Southwestern Railway. 
(3)	Silver Street, east side, from Butler Street north to Tyler Street. 
(4)	Dedicated alleys, running east and west between Tyler Street and Harrison Street, from Trinity Street to Henderson Street. 
(5)	Chandler Street, between Marshall Street and Butler Street, east side only. 
(6)	Spring Street, running north from Tyler Street parallel to the St. Louis and Southwestern Railway to Walnut Street. 
(7)	Dedicated alley, between Buffalo Street and Tyler Street from Trinity Street and north to Buffalo Street. 
(8)	Davis Street, on the west side, from Buffalo Street to Cass Street. 
(9)	Hollis Street, south side, from North Cypress Street to Silver Moon Cafe. 
(10)	Milburn Street, west side, from State Highway 300 south to Hilltop Avenue. 
(11)	Erwin Street, east side, from Hilltop Avenue south to Pattonfield Road. 
(12)	Warren Street, north side, from South Wood Street to Henderson Street. 
(13)	Titus Street, west side, from Madison Street north to Walker Street. 
(14)	North Titus Street, east side, from Redbud Street north to North Wood Street. 
(15)	Simpson Street, located parallel to and between Titus Street and Wood Street, running north from Cass Street to Taylor Street. 
(c)	Any vehicle parked in such areas designated no parking zones is in violation of subsection (b) and may be towed away and impounded. All charges for towing and storage shall be the responsibility of the owner of the vehicle. 
(Ord. No. 1983-0038, § 14.37, 12-22-1983) 
Sec. 86-201. - Provision for fines for violation. 
(a)	The city council or such other officer or employee as they may designate is authorized to issue a schedule of fines for violations of the provisions of this division. They are also authorized in their discretion to provide for additional penalties for repetitive offenders and delinquent offenders. 
(b)	For the purpose of this section, a repetitive offender means a person who commits five or more violations of this division within any 30-day period. 
(c)	For the purpose of this section, a delinquent offender means a person who fails to appear and answer to the charges of any violation of this division within the time period prescribed on the notice for the violation. 
(Ord. No. 1983-0038, § 14.39, 12-22-1983) 
Secs. 86-202—86-220. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 3. - SPECIFIC VEHICLES 
 
Sec. 86-221. - Vehicles over 1½ tons. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to leave, park or stand any truck tractor, road tractor, trailer, semitrailer, bus, trailer coach (trailer house), boats or RV's on streets or any commercial motor vehicle with a rated capacity of 1½ tons or more, according to the manufacturer's classification, or the equivalent, upon any public street, restricted public street in any area, alley, parkway, right-of-way, utility corridor, boulevard, lot, yard, public driveway, private driveway, city park or public park within or adjacent to any area zoned as either B-1 or B-2 in a residential area, single-family district R-1 or R-2 or RM-1 or RM-2 mobile home, or multifamily district MF-1 or MF-2, under this division. This section shall not prevent the parking or standing of such vehicles in such zoned areas for the purpose of expeditiously loading and unloading of passengers, freight or merchandise; but this section shall not apply to street construction, maintenance and repair equipment, such as trucks, rollers and implements or equipment, as well as trucks, trailers and vehicles used by public service utility companies engaged in repairing or extending public service utilities; and to motor buses when taking on or discharging passengers at customary bus stops. 
(Ord. No. 1999-007, 5-13-1999) 
Sec. 86-222. - Penalty. 
Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this division or fail to comply with any of its requirements shall be liable to a fine of not more than $500.00, and each day such violation shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. 1999-007, 5-13-1999) 
Secs. 86-223—86-240. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 4. - PERSONS WITH DISABILITIES 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (7) --- 
State Law reference— Administrative adjudication of parking regulations, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 682.001 et seq. 
Sec. 86-241. - Handicapped parking zones. 
(a)	In compliance with V.T.C.A., Transportation Code §§ 502.253, 681.001 et seq., the following provisions are adopted: 
(1)	There are designated two parking places for persons with disabilities directly in front of the Med-Shop Pharmacy, two parking places for persons with disabilities directly in front of Gilmer Walmart Store, and two parking places for persons with disabilities directly in front of Gilmer Brookshires Store. At no time may any vehicle other than that of a person with a disability be parked in any of these designated places. 
(2)	There are designated two parking places for persons with disabilities on the east side of the County Courthouse and one parking place for persons with disabilities on the east side of the Library Activities Building. 
(b)	Any person who violates any portion of subsection (a) of this section is also subject to the penalty provisions of section 1-14. Such offense is considered a class C misdemeanor. 
(c)	Any vehicle other than that of a person with a disability parked in such areas designated "HANDICAPPED PARKING" is in violation of subsection (a) and may be towed away and impounded. All charges for towing and storage shall be the responsibility of the owner of the vehicle. 
(Ord. No. 1990-006, § 14.43, 3-13-1990; Ord. No. 1992-006, § 14.44, 9-8-1992) 
Secs. 86-242—86-270. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE V. - TRUCK ROUTES  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Secs. 86-271—86-290. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - WEIGHT LIMITS ON SPECIFIC STREETS 
 
Sec. 86-291. - Truck traffic on Bruce Street. 
No through trucks exceeding three-quarter-ton capacity shall be driven on Bruce Street from its intersection with State Highway 300 to its intersection with State Highway 271. 
(Ord. No. 1987-008, § 14.10(A), 8-25-1987) 
Sec. 86-292. - Truck traffic on Cypress Street. 
No through trucks exceeding three-quarter-ton capacity shall be driven on Cypress Street from Highway 154 to Highway 155. 
(Ord. No. 1990-008, § 14.10(A), 6-12-1990) 
Sec. 86-293. - Truck traffic on Roberts Street. 
No through trucks exceeding three-quarter-ton capacity shall be driven on Roberts Street from Highway 154 to Highway 155. 
(Ord. No. 1990-009, § 14.10(A), 6-12-1990) 
Sec. 86-294. - Truck traffic on Butler Street. 
(a)	No through trucks exceeding three-quarter-ton capacity shall be driven on Butler Street from the intersection of Highway 271 to Roberts Street and on Roberts Street from the intersection of Highway 154 to Butler Street. 
(b)	Violation of this section by any person is declared to be a misdemeanor, and upon adjudication of guilt a fine not to exceed $200.00 shall be assessed against such violator. 
(Ord. No. 1995-0014, § 1, 6-22-1995) 
Secs. 86-295—86-320. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE VI. - RAILROADS 

FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (8) --- 
State Law reference— Railroads and railroad crossings, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 471.001 et seq. 
Sec. 86-321. - Maximum speed. 
It shall be unlawful for a person to operate, run or cause to be operated or run, within the corporate limits of the city, any railroad engine, car or train of cars at a greater rate of speed than 35 miles per hour. 
(Ord. No. 1986-0007, § 1, 9-11-1986) 
Sec. 86-322. - Audible warning required. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to conduct, run or cause to be run, any railroad engine, car or train of cars, approaching any street intersection within the city limits of the city, without sounding some audible warning device to warn vehicular traffic of the railroad engine, car or train of cars, to the crossing. 
(Ord. No. 1986-0007, § 2, 9-11-1986) 
Sec. 86-323. - Obstructing intersections. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any employee, officer, agent, servant or receiver of any railroad corporation to obstruct any street railway crossing or public highway within the city limits by permitting a train, including either the engine, car or train of cars, to obstruct or cross such street or crossing for more than ten minutes at any one time. 
(b)	An offense under this section is a misdemeanor punishable by a fine of not less than $100.00 or more than $300.00. 
(c)	An officer charging a railway company for an offense under this section shall prepare in duplicate a citation to appear in court and attach one copy of the citation to the train or deliver the copy to an employee or other agent of the railway company. The citation must show the: 
(1)	Name of the railway company;
(2)	Offense charged; and
(3)	Time and place that a representative of the railway company is to appear in court.
(d)	It is a defense to prosecution under this section that the train obstructs the street, railroad crossing or public highway because of an act of God or breakdown of the train. 
(e)	The hearing must be before a magistrate who has jurisdiction of the offense in the city. 
(f)	An appearance by counsel complies with the written promise to appear in court.
(Ord. No. 1986-0007, § 3, 9-11-1986)
State Law reference— Similar provisions, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 471.007.  
Sec. 86-324. - Maintenance of crossings. 
It shall be the duty of every railroad company at the crossing of its tracks with any avenue, street or highway within the city limits, to put and maintain the crossing in proper condition of repair for the entire width of the street at a place where it is crossed by the railroad tracks, in accordance with grades and by methods approved by the city engineer, and at its own costs and expense, maintain the crossing in a proper condition over the entire width of the designated passenger travel, and general use by the public. 
(Ord. No. 1986-0007, § 5, 9-11-1986) 
Sec. 86-325. - Jumping on or off, clinging to moving train. 
It shall be unlawful for any person, not being a regular passenger, employee or official of the railroad company, to jump on or off, to cling or to hang from or on to any railroad engine, car, or train of cars, while it is in motion. 
(Ord. No. 1986-0007, § 4, 9-11-1986) 
Chapter 90 - UTILITIES 
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (1) ---

Formerly, chapter 90 pertained to similar subject matter, and derived from Ord. No. 1990-005(1), § 11.55(A), adopted May 15, 1990; Ord. No. 1998-007, § 2, adopted July 27, 1998; Ord. No. 1998-013, §§ 1(1)(A—D), (2)(A—M), (2.1), (3.0)(A—L), (3.1)(A—C), (4)(A—F), (4.1)(A), (4.2)(A, B), (4.3)(A—D), (4.4)(A—F), adopted December 10, 1998; Ord. No. 2000-002, §§ I—XII, adopted March 9, 2000; Ord. No. 2001-007, adopted September 11, 2001; Ord. No. 2001-007A, adopted September 19, 2002; Ord. No. 2002-007, adopted September 19, 2002; Ord.
